Life of Imam Ibn Asakir
beginner
5 min
Imam al-Ghazali's Return to Teaching and Final Years
Ibn Asakir narrates Ghazali's return to teaching, his daily routine, opposition, focus on hadith, and death.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Imam al-Ghazali balanced teaching, spiritual practice, and faced opposition in his later years, culminating in his focus on hadith and his death.

Core Idea
Ghazali's return to teaching was a religious duty, and his final years were dedicated to hadith and spiritual community.

After his spiritual transformation, Ghazali was called back to teach in Nishapur. He felt it was his duty to proclaim the truth. However, he eventually left that role and built a school and Sufi lodge near his home. He faced slander and opposition but remained protected. In his final days, he turned to the study of hadith, particularly the Sahihs of Bukhari and Muslim, and would have excelled further if he had lived longer. He died content with little, refusing worldly wealth.

Guided Path
1
Read Ghazali's answer about leaving home
When asked why he returned to Nishapur, Ghazali said it was his religious duty to call to truth and benefit seekers.
He was truthful in this.
2
Observe his new routine and institutions
He built a madrasa and a khanaqah, dividing his time between Quran, spiritual company, and teaching.
Every moment was fruitful.
3
Note the opposition he faced
He was targeted by adversaries and slandered to kings, but Allah protected him.
4
Focus on his turn to hadith at the end
In his final days, he dedicated himself to studying Bukhari and Muslim, and would have surpassed others in hadith if he lived longer.
He left many books but not in hadith transmission.
5
Learn about his death and character
He died in 505 AH, buried near Tabaran. He was content with little and refused wealth.
He left only daughters.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
البسطة في النطق والخاطر والعبارة ، وطلب الجاه والعلو في المنزلة أنه صار على الضد وتصفى عن تلك الكدورات وكنت أظن أنه متلفع بجلباب التكلف متنمس بما صار إليه فتحققت بعد السبر والتنقير أن الأمر على خلاف المظنون ، وأن الرجل أفاق بعد الجنون وحكى لنا في ليال كيفية أحواله من ابتداء ما ظهر له سلوك طريق التأله وغلبت الحال عليه بعد تبحره في العلوم واستطالته على الكل بكلامه والاستعداد الذي خصه الله به به فی تحصيل أنواع العلوم وتمكنه من البحث والنظر حتي تبرم من الاشتغال بالعلوم العربية عن المعاملة وتفكر في العاقبة وما يجرى وينفع في الآخرة فابتدأ بصحبة الفارمذى وأخذ منه استفتاح الطريقة وامتثل ما كان يشير به عليه من القيام بوظائف العبادات والامعان في النوافل واستدامة الأذكار والجد والاجتهاد طلباً للنجاة إلى أن جاز تلك العقبات وتكلف تلك المشاق وما تحصل على ما كان يطلبه من مقصوده ، ثم حكى أنه راجع العلوم وخاض فى الفنون وعاود الجد والاجتهاد في كتب العلوم الدقيقة والتقى بأربابها حتي انفتح له أبوابها وبقى مدة في الوقائع وتكافئ الأدلة وأطراف المسائل ثم حكى أنه فتح عليه باب من الخوف بحيث شغله كل شئ وحمله على الإعراض عما سواه حتى سهل ذلك وهكذا إلى أن أرتاض كل الرياضة وظهرت له الحقائق وصار ما كنا نظن به ناموساً وتخلقا طبعاً وتحققا وأن ذلك أثر السعادة المقدرة له من الله تعالى ثم سألناه عن كيفية رغبته في الخروج من بيته والرجوع إلى ما دعى إليه من أمر نيسابور فقال معتذرا عنه ما كنت أجوز في ديني أن أقف عن الدعوة ومنفعة الطالبين بالافادة وقد حق على أن أبوح بالحق وأنطق به وأدعو إليه ، وكان صادقاً في ذلك ثم ترك ذلك قبل أن يترك وعاد إلى بيته وأتخذ في جواره مدرسة لطلبة العلم وخانقاه للصوفية ، وكان قد وزع أوقاته على وظائف الحاضرين من ختم القرآن ومجالسة أهل القلوب ، والقعود للتدريس بحيث لا تخلو لحظة من لحظاته ولحظات من معه عن فائدة ، إلى أن أصابه عين الزمان وضن الأنام به على أهل عصره فنقله الله إلى كريم جواره بعد مقاساة أنواع من القصد والمناوأة من الخصوم والسعى به إلى الملوك وكفاية الله تعالى وحفظه وصيانته عن أن تنوشه أيدى النكبات أو ينهتك ستر دینه بشئ من الزلات ، وكانت خاتمة أمره إقباله على حديث المصطفى صلى الله عليه وسلم ومجالسة أهله ومطالعة الصحيحين البخاري ومسلم اللذين هما حجة الإسلام ولو عاش لسبق الكل في ذلك الفن بيسير من الأيام يستفرغه في تحصيله ، ولا شك أنه سمع الأحاديث في الأيام الماضية واشتغل في آخر عمره بسماعها ولم تتفق له الرواية ولا ضرر فيما خلفه من الكتب المصنفة في الأصول والفروع وسائر الأنواع يخلد ذكره ويقررر عند المطالعين المنصفين المستفيدين منها أنه لم يخلف مثله بعده ، ومضى إلى رحمة الله تعالى يوم الاثنين الرابع عشر من جمادى الآخرة سنة خمس وخمسمائة ودفن بظاهر قصبة طابران ، والله تعالى يخصه بأنواع الكرامة في آخرته كما خصه بفنون العلم في دنياه بمنه ، ولم يعقب إلا البنات وكان له من الأسباب إرثا وكسبا ما يقوم بكفايته ونفقة أهله وأولاده فما كان يباسط أحدا في الأمور الدنيوية وقد عرضت عليه أموال فما قبلها وأعرض عنها واكتفى بالقدر الذي يصون به دينه ولا يحتاج معه إلى التعرض لسؤال ومنال من غيره .
Fluency in speech, thought, and expression, and seeking status and high rank made him become opposite and purified from those turbidities. I used to think he was wrapped in the cloak of affectation, submerged in what he had become, but after investigation and scrutiny I realized the matter was contrary to what was presumed, and that the man had recovered after madness. He narrated to us over several nights the manner of his states from the beginning of what appeared to him of following the path of devotion (tā'allah), and the state prevailing over him after his deep immersion in the sciences, and his superiority over everyone with his speech, and the capacity that Allah had specially given him in acquiring various types of knowledge, and his mastery of research and reflection, until he became weary of occupying himself with the Arabic sciences over spiritual practice (muʿāmala). He reflected on the final outcome and what would benefit in the Hereafter. So he began accompanying al-Fāramadhī and took from him the commencement of the path (ṭarīqa). He complied with what he advised him regarding performing the duties of worship, diligence in supererogatory acts, continuity of dhikr, and earnest striving in seeking salvation, until he crossed those obstacles and undertook those hardships, yet he did not attain what he sought of his goal. Then he narrated that he returned to the sciences and delved into the arts, and resumed earnestness and diligence in the books of the subtle sciences, meeting their masters until their doors opened to him. He remained for a period in [dealing with] events, the parity of evidences, and the extremities of issues. Then he narrated that a door of fear was opened for him such that it occupied him with everything and caused him to turn away from all else until that became easy. Thus he continued until he was completely trained, the realities appeared to him, and what we had thought to be a mere veneer and acquired trait became natural and realized, and that was the effect of the happiness decreed for him by Allah Almighty. Then we asked him about the manner of his desire to leave his home and return to what he had been called to concerning the affair of Nishapur. He apologized, saying: 'I would not allow in my religion to refrain from the call and benefiting the seekers by teaching, and it is incumbent upon me to proclaim the truth, speak it, and call to it.' He was truthful in that. Then he left it before it left him, and returned to his home, and built adjacent to it a school (madrasa) for students of knowledge and a khānaqāh for the Sufis. He divided his times among the functions for those present: completing the Qur'an, sitting with people of hearts, and sitting for teaching, such that not a moment of his moments or of those with him was devoid of benefit. Until the evil eye of time befell him, and people begrudged him to the people of his era, so Allah transferred him to His generous neighborhood after enduring various types of targeting and opposition from adversaries, and being slandered to kings, but Allah Almighty sufficed, protected, and preserved him from the hands of calamities reaching him or the veil of his religion being torn by any slip. The end of his affair was his turning to the hadith of the Chosen One (peace be upon him), sitting with its people, studying the two Sahihs of Bukhari and Muslim, which are the proof of Islam. Had he lived, he would have surpassed everyone in that art in a few days which he would expend to acquire it. There is no doubt that he heard hadiths in past days and occupied himself in the last part of his life with listening to them, but he did not have the opportunity for narration. There is no harm in what he left behind of authored books in uṣūl, furūʿ, and all types – they immortalize his mention and confirm in the view of fair-minded readers who benefit from them that he left no like after him. He passed away to the mercy of Allah Almighty on Monday, the fourteenth of Jumādā al-Ākhira in the year five hundred and five, and was buried outside the town of Ṭābarān. May Allah Almighty bestow upon him various kinds of honor in his Hereafter as He specially favored him with types of knowledge in his worldly life, by His bounty. He left behind only daughters. He had from means, inheritance and earnings, what sufficed for his maintenance and the expenses of his family and children. He never negotiated with anyone in worldly matters; wealth was offered to him but he did not accept it and turned away from it, content with the amount that protects his religion and with which he does not need to expose himself to asking or receiving from others.
Source pages p. 226

Commentary
This passage is a biographical narrative of Imam al-Ghazali, as related by Ibn Asakir. It describes his spiritual journey and transformation. The narrator initially believed Ghazali's state was affected, but after investigation realized it was genuine. Ghazali, after excelling in sciences, became weary of worldly learning and turned to asceticism, accompanying the Sufi master al-Fāramadhī. He struggled in the path but did not attain his goal immediately. He then returned to the sciences with renewed vigor, eventually opening the door of fear of Allah, which led him to turn away from everything else. He was asked why he left his home to return to teaching in Nishapur; he answered that it was his religious duty to call to truth and benefit others. After a period, he left that position and built a school and khānaqāh near his home, devoting his time to Quran recitation, spiritual company, and teaching. He faced opposition and slander but was protected by Allah. At the end of his life, he focused on hadith, studying Bukhari and Muslim, and would have excelled if he had lived longer. He died in 505 AH, buried outside Tabaran. He was content with little, refusing wealth offered to him.

Key Terms
الصحيحين
خانقاه
مدرسة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Ghazali stopped teaching after his spiritual crisis.
Correction: He returned to teaching as a duty and built a madrasa and khanaqah.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what did Ghazali build near his home?
A) A mosque
B) A madrasa and a khanaqah
C) A library
D) A hospital

Key Takeaway
Imam al-Ghazali's later years were marked by his return to teaching, building a school and Sufi lodge, facing opposition, and dedicating his final days to the study of hadith.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Ghazali considered it a religious duty to teach and benefit others, even after leaving public life. Is there an area of knowledge or skill you possess that you have been neglecting to share with others? What is stopping you from fulfilling that duty today?
?
Ghazali refused wealth offered to him, content with enough to protect his religion. Examine your own relationship with money and possessions: Where might you be compromising your faith for financial gain or comfort? What step can you take this week to simplify your life and strengthen your reliance on Allah?
?
Towards the end of his life, Ghazali devoted himself completely to the study of hadith. If you knew your time on earth was short, what would you prioritize learning or practicing? Why not begin that priority today?

Life of Imam Ibn Asakir
beginner
5 min
A Scholar's Devotion to Hadith and Asceticism
Biographical notice of a scholar's virtues and death.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the character and scholarly legacy of a pious hadith scholar who died in 505 AH.

Core Idea
True scholars seek knowledge for Allah, not worldly gain.

This passage from Ibn 'Asakir's Tabyin introduces a scholar whose life was defined by love for the Sunnah and detachment from worldly wealth. His study of al-Sahihayn and his contentment with sufficiency provide a model for students of sacred knowledge. Let us examine his biography and reflect on his virtues.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing it, then read the full English translation. Notice the tone and the virtues highlighted.
2
Identify the scholar's main activities
The passage mentions studying the Sahihayn, sitting with the people of hadith, and listening to hadith in his later years. Also note that he did not become a narrator.
3
Observe his attitude toward wealth
The scholar refused offered wealth and was content with enough to preserve his religion. He did not engage in worldly discussions.
This shows his asceticism (zuhd).
4
Reflect on his legacy
He left behind books in various disciplines and daughters who inherited his means. The author says his mention will be immortalized.
His legacy is intellectual and spiritual, not material.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
صلى الله عليه وسلم ومجالسة أهله ومطالعة الصحيحين البخاري ومسلم اللذين هما حجة الإسلام ولو عاش لسبق الكل في ذلك الفن بيسير من الأيام يستفرغه في تحصيله ، ولا شك أنه سمع الأحاديث في الأيام الماضية واشتغل في آخر عمره بسماعها ولم تتفق له الرواية ولا ضرر فيما خلفه من الكتب المصنفة في الأصول والفروع وسائر الأنواع يخلد ذكره ويقرر عند المطالعين المنصفين المستفيدين منها أنه لم يخلف مثله بعده ، ومضى إلى رحمة الله تعالى يوم الاثنين الرابع عشر من جمادى الآخرة سنة خمس وخمسمائة ودفن بظاهر قصبة طابران ، والله تعالى يخصه بأنواع الكرامة في آخرته كما خصه بفنون العلم في دنياه بمنه ، ولم يعقب إلا البنات وكان له من الأسباب إرثا وكسبا ما يقوم بكفايته ونفقة أهله وأولاده فما كان يباسط أحدا في الأمور الدنيوية وقد عرضت عليه أموال فما قبلها وأعرض عنها واكتفى بالقدر الذي يصون به دينه ولا يحتاج معه إلى التعرض لسؤال ومنال من غيره .
May Allah bless him and grant him peace, and sitting with his people, and studying the two Sahihs of Bukhari and Muslim which are the proof of Islam, and if he had lived he would have preceded everyone in that art in a few days which he would spend to acquire it. There is no doubt that he heard hadiths in the past days and occupied himself in the last part of his life with hearing them, and narration was not granted to him, and there is no harm in what he left behind of books classified in principles and branches and all types; his mention will be immortalized and it will be established with fair-minded readers who benefit from them that he left no one like him after him. He passed on to the mercy of Allah Almighty on Monday, the fourteenth of Jumada al-Akhirah in the year five hundred and five, and was buried on the outskirts of the citadel of Tabaran. And Allah Almighty will grant him varieties of honor in his hereafter as He granted him varieties of knowledge in this world by His grace. He left behind only daughters, and he had from means, inheritance and earnings, what sufficed for his sustenance and the expenses of his family and children. He did not engage anyone in worldly matters, and wealth was offered to him but he did not accept it and turned away from it, and he was content with the amount that preserves his religion and does not need to expose himself to asking or receiving from others.
Source pages p. 227

Commentary
This passage is a biographical notice about a scholar who died in 505 AH. It begins by describing his close association with the people of hadith and his study of the two authentic collections (al-Sahihayn) of Bukhari and Muslim, which are considered the proof of Islam. It then states that if he had lived longer, he would have surpassed all others in that field within a short time. The passage notes that he spent his later years listening to hadiths even though he did not become a narrator, and that the books he left behind in various disciplines ensure his lasting legacy. It then gives his death date and burial place (outside the citadel of Tabaran). It emphasizes his piety: Allah honored him with knowledge in this world and will honor him in the hereafter. He left only daughters, but his inheritance and earnings sufficed for his family. He refused wealth offered to him and was content with enough to preserve his religion, avoiding asking from others.

Key Terms
الصحيحين
البخاري
مسلم
قصبة طابران

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: A scholar's value depends on having a chain of narration (riwayah).
Correction: The scholar did not become a narrator, but his written works in principles and branches established his legacy, showing that teaching and writing are also valuable.

Checkpoint
What year did the scholar described in this passage die?
A) 505 AH
B) 515 AH
C) 495 AH
D) 525 AH

Key Takeaway
This scholar combined deep study of hadith with asceticism, leaving a legacy of books and a model of pious contentment.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
You are offered a large sum of money to stop studying a religious text for a week. Would you take it? How does the scholar's refusal of wealth challenge your own struggles with worldly distractions?
?
What 'books' are you leaving behind—not physical pages, but the impact of your knowledge and character on those after you? If you died today, would anyone say you left a legacy like his?
?
The scholar was content with just enough to 'preserve his religion'. Are you content with your provision, or do you constantly seek more? Ask yourself honestly: does your pursuit of wealth ever compromise your faith?

Life of Imam Ibn Asakir

The Dream of al-Ghazali and the Prophet
Ibn Asakir recounts a dream in which al-Ghazali recites Qawā‘id al-‘Aqā’id before the Prophet.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the significance of Ibn 'Asākir's dream about al-Ghazali and its role in validating the Ash'ari creed.

Core Idea
A dream where the Prophet smiles at al-Ghazali's creed confirms its truth.

In this lesson, we read a remarkable dream narrative from Ibn 'Asākir's defense of al-Ghazali. The author relates that while reciting the description of the Prophet from Qawā'id al-'Aqā'id, the Prophet himself appears, calls al-Ghazali, and shows delight at his work. This dream serves as a powerful confirmation of the creed and a source of comfort for believers.

Guided Path
1
Read the dream narrative
Carefully read the Arabic passage and its translation. Notice the emotional language and the detailed description of the Prophet's reaction.
2
Identify key elements
Identify the recitation of the Prophet's attributes, the Prophet's smile, the appearance of al-Ghazali, and his gesture of kissing the Prophet's hand.
The author emphasises the Prophet's delight at al-Ghazali's work.
3
Reflect on the theological role of dreams
Consider that in Islamic tradition, dreams can be confirmatory but are not sources of law. How does this dream function?
It validates the creed of Ahl al-Ḥaqq.
4
Consider the author's prayer
Read the concluding prayer for steadfastness. Why does the author include this prayer after the dream?
It shows the dream's purpose: to encourage firmness in faith.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
معنى الكلمة الثانية وهي شهادة أن محمداً رسول الله أنه تعالى بعث النبي الأمي القرشي محمداً صلى الله عليه وسلم برسالته إلى كافة العرب والعجم والجن والإنس قال فلما بلغت إلى هذا رأيت البشاشة والتبسم في وجهه صلى الله عليه وسلم إذ انتهيت إلى نعته وصفته فالتفت إلى وقال أين الغزالي فإذا بالغزالي كأنه كان واقفا على الحلقة بين يديه، فقال هاأنذا يا رسول الله وتقدم وسلم على رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم فرد عليه الجواب وناوله يده العزيزة والغزالي يقبل يده ويضع خديه عليها تبركاً به وبيده العزيزة المباركة ، ثم قعد قال فما رأيت رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم أكثر استبشارا بقراءة أحد مثل ما كان بقراءتي عليه قواعد العقائد ثم انتبهت من النوم وعلى عيني أثر الدمع مما رأيت من تلك الأحوال والمشاهدات والكرامات فإنها كانت نعمة جسيمة من الله تعالى سيما في آخر الزمان مع كثرة الأهواء ، فنسأل الله تعالى أن يثبتنا على عقيدة أهل الحق ويحيينا ويميتنا عليها ، ويحشرنا معهم ومع الأنبياء والمرسلين والصديقين والشهداء والصالحين وحسن أولئك رفيقا، فإنه بالفضل جدير وعلى ما يشاء قدير .
The meaning of the second word (al-kalima) — which is the testimony that Muhammad is the Messenger of Allah — is that He, exalted, sent the unlettered Qurayshi prophet Muhammad, peace be upon him, with His message to all Arabs, non-Arabs, jinn, and humans. He said: When I reached this point, I saw cheerfulness and a smile on his face, peace be upon him, when I completed his description and attribute. He turned to me and said: 'Where is al-Ghazali?' And lo, al-Ghazali was as if standing at the circle before him. He said: 'Here I am, O Messenger of Allah.' He stepped forward and greeted the Messenger of Allah, peace be upon him, who returned the greeting and gave him his noble hand, and al-Ghazali kissed his hand and placed his cheeks upon it, seeking blessing from him and his noble blessed hand. Then he sat down. He said: I have never seen the Messenger of Allah, peace be upon him, more delighted with anyone's recitation than he was with my recitation of Qawā‘id al-‘Aqā’id to him. Then I woke up from my sleep with traces of tears on my eyes because of what I had seen of those states, visions, and miracles (karāmāt). For it was a great blessing from Allah, especially in these later times with the abundance of desires. So we ask Allah to make us firm on the creed of the people of truth, to let us live and die upon it, and to resurrect us with them and with the prophets, the truthful, the martyrs, and the righteous — excellent are those as companions. For He is worthy of grace and powerful over what He wills.
Source pages p. 232

Commentary
This passage is a narrative of a dream (ru’yā) experienced by the author (Ibn ‘Asākir). The dream involves the Prophet Muhammad approving of al-Ghazali and his work 'Qawā‘id al-‘Aqā’id'. The author describes that while reciting the attributes of the Prophet in the creed, the Prophet smiled and asked for al-Ghazali, who then came forward, greeted the Prophet, and kissed his hand. The Prophet showed great delight at the recitation of al-Ghazali's work. The author wakes up with tears, seeing this as a blessing and a confirmation of the creed. He concludes with a prayer for steadfastness on the creed of Ahl al-Ḥaqq. This narrative serves to validate the Ash‘ari creed and the work of al-Ghazali as being pleasing to the Prophet.

Key Terms
رؤيا
تبشير
قواعد العقائد
غزالي

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Dreams are not authoritative in religious matters.
Correction: This dream serves as a confirmatory sign, not a source of law, and shows the Prophet's approval of al-Ghazali's creed.

Checkpoint
What did the Prophet do when al-Ghazali recited Qawā‘id al-‘Aqā’id?
A) He corrected him.
B) He showed delight.
C) He remained silent.
D) He asked him to stop.

Key Takeaway
This dream narrative affirms the Prophet's approval of al-Ghazali's creed and encourages steadfastness in the face of desires.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If the Prophet were to attend your recitation of a creedal text today, would he smile? What would he see in your heart that differs from what you recite with your tongue?
?
The dream caused Ibn Asakir to weep tears of joy and fear. When was the last time the truth of the creed moved you to tears? Do you feel that same firmness, or are you drifting with your desires?
?
You claim to follow the creed of Ahl al-Sunna, but do you live it? Imagine waking up from a dream like this—would your reaction be gratitude or indifference? Ask yourself: is your faith strong enough to be confirmed by such a vision, or would you be ashamed?

Al-Ghazali's Dream of Reciting to the Prophet
Ibn Asakir narrates al-Ghazali's dream of reading Qawa'id al-Aqa'id to the Prophet.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the significance of al-Ghazali's dream as a validation of his creedal work and the concept of miraculous visions (karamat) in Islam.

Core Idea
A dream can confirm the truth of a scholar's teaching.

This lesson presents a remarkable dream of Imam al-Ghazali, in which he recites his work on creed to the Prophet Muhammad (peace be upon him) and receives his joyful approval. The dream serves both as a personal blessing and as a testament to the correctness of the creedal principles outlined in his book. As you read, note the emotional tone and the doctrinal underpinnings.

Guided Path
1
Read the narrative
Read the full Arabic passage and its translation carefully. Observe the vivid details of the dream.
The passage is a first-person account by al-Ghazali.
2
Notice the Prophet's reaction
Pay attention to the Prophet's exceptional joy and his statement that he had never been so joyful at anyone's recitation.
This is the key validation of al-Ghazali's work.
3

Al-Ghazali ends with a prayer for steadfastness on the creed of truth. Consider the humility and hope expressed.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
معنى الكلمة الثانية وهي شهادة الرسول الله أنه تعالى بعث النبي الأمى القرشي محمداً ﷺ برسالته إلى كافة العرب والعجم والجن والأنس قال فلما بلغت إلى هذا رأيت البشاشة والتبسم في وجهه ﷺ إذ انتهيت إلى نعته وصفته فالتفت إلى وقال أين الغزالي فإذا بالغزالي كأنه كان واقفا على الحلقة بين يديه، فقال هانا ذا يا رسول الله وتقدم وسلم على رسول الله ﷺ فرد عليه الجواب وناوله يده العزيزة والغزالي يقبل يده ويضع خديه عليها تبركاً به وبيده العزيزة المباركة ، ثم قعد قال فما رأيت رسول الله ﷺ أكثر استبشارا بقراءة أحد مثل ما كان بقراءتي عليه قواعد العقائد ثم انتبهت من النوم وعلى عينى أثر الدمع مما رأيت من تلك الأحوال والمشاهدات والكرامات فإنها كانت نعمة جسيمة : من الله تعالى سيما في آخر الزمان مع كثرة الأهواء ، فنسأل الله تعالى أن يثبتنا على عقيدة أهل الحق ويحيينا ويميتنا عليها ، ويحشرنا معهم ومع الأنبياء والمرسلين والصديقين والشهداء والصالحين وحسن أولئك رفيقا، فإنه بالفضل جدير وعلى ما يشاء قدير
The meaning of the second word, which is the testimony of the Messenger of Allah, that He, exalted, sent the unlettered Qurayshi prophet Muhammad, may Allah bless him and grant him peace, with His message to all Arabs and non-Arabs and jinn and humans. He said: When I reached this point, I saw cheerfulness and smile on his face, peace be upon him, when I came to his description and attribute. So he turned to me and said: 'Where is al-Ghazali?' And lo, al-Ghazali was standing at the circle before him. He said: 'Here I am, O Messenger of Allah,' and he came forward and greeted the Messenger of Allah, peace be upon him. He returned the greeting and extended his noble hand, and al-Ghazali was kissing his hand and placing his cheeks upon it, seeking blessing from him and his noble blessed hand. Then he sat down. He said: I have not seen the Messenger of Allah, peace be upon him, more joyful at anyone's recitation than he was at my recitation of Qawa'id al-Aqa'id to him. Then I awoke from sleep, and on my eyes were traces of tears from what I saw of those states and visions and miracles, for it was a great blessing from Allah, especially in the end times amidst the multitude of desires. So we ask Allah to make us firm upon the creed of the people of truth, and to give us life and death upon it, and to gather us with them and with the prophets, the truthful, the martyrs, and the righteous—excellent are those as companions. For He is worthy of bounty and powerful over what He wills.
Source pages p. 232

Commentary
This passage is a first-person narrative of a dream experienced by al-Ghazali. It begins by connecting to the earlier discussion of the second pillar of testimony, that Muhammad is the Messenger of Allah. While reciting the description of the Prophet from his work Qawa'id al-Aqa'id, al-Ghazali sees the Prophet's face brighten. The Prophet asks for al-Ghazali, who comes forward, greets him, and is honored by shaking and kissing the Prophet's hand. The Prophet expresses exceptional joy at the recitation, more than at anyone else's. Al-Ghazali then wakes up weeping, viewing the dream as a great blessing and a miracle, especially in later times of conflicting desires. He concludes with a supplication for steadfastness on the truth and for a good ending in the company of the righteous.

Correction: The passage treats the dream as a true vision (ru'ya) and a karamah, not a physical encounter. Visions of the Prophet are considered valid in Sunni Islam.

Scholarly Testimony and the Dream of al-Ghazali
Al-Isfara'ini confirms a dream, adding a translation note.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how a scholar's testimony and translation authenticate a dream narrative in the Islamic tradition.

Core Idea
Scholarly testimony bridges languages and confirms spiritual experiences.

This short passage presents a scholar's direct confirmation of a dream regarding al-Ghazali. Imam Abu al-Qasim al-Isfara'ini states that he personally received the account in Persian from Abu al-Fath al-Sawi and then rendered it into Arabic. This illustrates the care early scholars took to preserve and transmit even dream narratives with a clear chain of transmission.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage and translation
Start by reading the Arabic sentence aloud, then compare with the literal translation. Notice the structure: a statement of meaning, a chain of narration, and a note on translation.
The passage is a single continuous statement.
2
Identify the chain of narrators
Trace the transmission: Abu al-Fath al-Sawi saw the dream and narrated it to al-Isfara'ini. Al-Isfara'ini then confirms its meaning and provides the Arabic version.
This chain adds credibility to the dream account.
3
Observe the language shift
Notice that the original narration was in Persian, but the scholar translated it into Arabic. Think about why this translation was necessary for wider dissemination.
Arabic was the scholarly lingua franca.
4
Reflect on the purpose of this testimony
Ask yourself why al-Isfara'ini felt the need to explicitly confirm the dream. Consider that dreams of saints were often cited as evidence of spiritual status, and authentication was important.
The common misunderstanding is that such dreams might be fabricated.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال الشيخ الإمام أبو القسم الاسفرايني هذا معنى ما حكى لي أبو الفتح الساوى أنه رآه في المنام لأنه حكاه لي بالفارسية وترجمته أنا بالعربية
Shaykh Imam Abu al-Qasim al-Isfara'ini said: This is the meaning of what Abu al-Fath al-Sawi narrated to me, that he saw it in the dream, because he narrated it to me in Persian and I translated it into Arabic.
Source pages p. 233

Commentary
This short passage is a testimonial from Imam Abu al-Qasim al-Isfara'ini, a prominent Ash'ari theologian. He states that the account of al-Ghazali's dream, which was communicated to him in Persian by Abu al-Fath al-Sawi, is accurate. Al-Isfara'ini himself rendered it into Arabic, confirming the narrative's authenticity and providing a chain of transmission.

Misconception: That the dream account was fabricated or lacked evidence.

Biography of Imam Abu Bakr al-Shashi
Ibn Asakir provides a brief biography of Imam Abu Bakr al-Shashi, a Shafi'i scholar.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the life and scholarly contributions of Imam Abu Bakr al-Shashi as recorded by Ibn Asakir.

Core Idea
Imam Abu Bakr al-Shashi was a leading Shafi'i jurist who taught at the Nizamiyya and authored many works.

In this passage, Ibn Asakir introduces us to one of the great Shafi'i scholars of Baghdad: Imam Abu Bakr al-Shashi. We learn about his teachers, his role as a repetitor (mu'id), his appointment at the prestigious Nizamiyya school, and his many students. This biographical notice gives us a glimpse into the chain of scholarly transmission that defined Islamic learning.

Guided Path
1
Read the biographical passage
Read the Arabic passage and its translation to get a first impression of Imam al-Shashi's life and accomplishments.

These details form the core of a traditional biographical entry.
3
Reflect on scholarly transmission
Reflect on how the passage shows the chain of learning: from Abu Ishaq al-Shirazi to al-Shashi, and from al-Shashi to his students.
This exemplifies the Islamic tradition of isnad and scholarly lineage.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ومنهم الإمام أبو بكر الشاشي رحمه الله ) واسمه محمد بن أحمد بن الحسين . تفقه على الشيخ أبي إسحاق الشيرازي وغيره ، وكان معيداً له وولى التدريس بالمدرسة النظامية وغيرها ببغداد، وله تصانيف كثيرة حسنة وتفقه به جماعة أئمة كالقاضي الإمام أبي العباس بن الرطبي وابنه أبى المظفر وأبي محمد ابنى أبي بكر وغيرهم وذكر شيخنا الشيخ أبو محمد بن الأكفاني أنه مات في يوم السبت الخامس والعشرين من شوال سنة سبع وسبعين وخمسمائة قال وإليه انتهت الرئاسة لأصحاب الشافعي رحمة الله عليه ببغداد
And among them is Imam Abu Bakr al-Shashi (may Allah have mercy on him) – his name is Muhammad ibn Ahmad ibn al-Husayn. He studied fiqh under Shaykh Abu Ishaq al-Shirazi and others, and was his repetitor (mu'id). He was appointed to teaching at the Nizamiyya school and others in Baghdad. He has many good compositions (tasannif). A group of imams studied fiqh under him, such as Qadi Imam Abu al-Abbas ibn al-Rutbi and his son Abu al-Muzaffar, and Abu Muhammad ibn Abi Bakr, and others. Our teacher Shaykh Abu Muhammad ibn al-Akfani mentioned that he died on Saturday, the 25th of Shawwal, in the year 577 AH. He said: And to him ended the leadership of the Shafi'is in Baghdad.
Source pages p. 234

Commentary
This passage is a biographical notice on Imam Abu Bakr al-Shashi. It begins by stating his name: Muhammad ibn Ahmad ibn al-Husayn. He studied fiqh under the famous Shafi'i jurist Abu Ishaq al-Shirazi and others, and served as his repetitor (mu'id – one who repeats the teacher's lessons). He was appointed to teach at the Nizamiyya school in Baghdad, a prestigious institution, as well as other schools. He authored many good works (tasannif). A number of leading imams studied fiqh under him, including Qadi Abu al-Abbas ibn al-Rutbi, his son Abu al-Muzaffar, and Abu Muhammad ibn Abi Bakr, among others. The passage then records his death date from Shaykh Abu Muhammad ibn al-Akfani: Saturday, 25th Shawwal 577 AH. The biographer notes that leadership of the Shafi'i school in Baghdad culminated with him.

أبو إسحاق الشيرازي

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ومنهم الإمام أبو القسم الأنصاری النیسابوری رحمه الله ) سمعت الشيخ أبا بكر محمد بن عبد الله بن حبيب الفقيه العامري ببغداد وثنا عنه بحديث يحسن عليه الثناء ويقول : كان عالماً إماماً في التفسير والأصول . وذكر الشيخ أبو الحسن عبد الغافر بن إسماعيل فيما كتب إلى قال : سلمان بن ناصر بن عمران بن محمد بن إسماعيل بن إسحق ابن يزيد بن زياد أبو القسم الانصارى الإمام الدين الورع الزاهد فريد عصره

And Shaykh Abu al-Hasan Abd al-Ghafir ibn Isma'il mentioned in what he wrote to me, saying: Salman ibn Nasir ibn Imran ibn Muhammad ibn Isma'il ibn Ishaq ibn Yazid ibn Ziyad Abu al-Qasim al-Ansari – the imam, the religious, the pious, the ascetic, the unique of his time.

The Scholar and Ascetic: Imam Abu al-Qasim al-Ansari al-Naysaburi
Ibn Asakir describes al-Ansari's scholarship, asceticism, and precision in kalam.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Imam al-Ansari combined deep scholarship in tafsir, usul, and kalam with asceticism and Sufi practice, demonstrating that theological precision and personal piety are compatible.

Core Idea
A scholar of kalam can also be a devout ascetic and Sufi.

Ibn Asakir introduces us to a remarkable figure who mastered both the rational sciences of kalam and the spiritual path of Sufism. This biography shows that deep theological precision and personal piety are not only compatible but complementary. The passage includes direct testimony from two sources, praising al-Ansari's unique status.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once, then the English translation. Notice how the description builds from a brief praise to a detailed portrait.
The passage opens with a chain of transmission, establishing credibility.
2
Identify the praised qualities
List the attributes mentioned: being an imam in tafsir and usul, knowledge of the spiritual path (tariqa), precedence in Sufism, precise insight, integrity, and awareness of the imams' ways in kalam.
These qualities cover both exoteric sciences and esoteric practice.
3
Notice the balance between knowledge and practice
The text emphasizes that his knowledge surpassed his speech, showing that his inner state was deeper than his outward expression. Reflect on the mention of his living like the pious on the conduct of the salaf.
This balance is a key theme: he was not just a theoretician but a practitioner.
4
Reflect on the limitation of speech
Despite his deep knowledge, he had a limitation in verbal articulation. Consider what this teaches about the relationship between knowledge and expression.
It reminds us that true knowledge is not always eloquent but sincere.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ومنهم الإمام أبو القسم الأنصاری النیسابوری رحمه الله ) سمعت الشيخ أبا بكر محمد بن عبد الله بن حبيب الفقيه العامري ببغداد وثنا عنه بحديث يحسن عليه الثناء ويقول : كان عالماً إماماً في التفسير والأصول . وذكر الشيخ أبو الحسن عبد الغافر بن إسماعيل فيما كتب إلى قال : سلمان بن ناصر بن عمران بن محمد بن إسماعيل بن إسحق ابن يزيد بن زياد أبو القسم الانصارى الإمام الدين الورع الزاهد فريد عصره في فنه ، وكان له معرفة بالطريقة وقدم فى التصوف ونظر دقيق وفكر في المعاملة وتصاون في النفس وعفاف في الطعم ، وكان حسن الطريقة دقيق النظر واقفاً على مسالك الأئمة وطرقهم في علم الكلام بصيراً بمواعظ الأشكال، مع قصور في تقرير لسانه وكانت معرفته فوق نطقه ومعناه أوفر من ظاهره وفحواه ، و عاش عيش الأبرار على سيرة السلف الصالحين وتوفى صبيحة يوم الخـ الثاني والعشرين من جمادى الآخرة سنة أثنتى عشرة وخمسمائة
And among them is Imam Abu al-Qasim al-Ansari al-Naysaburi (may God have mercy on him). I heard Shaykh Abu Bakr Muhammad ibn 'Abd Allah ibn Habib al-Faqih al-'Amiri in Baghdad, and he narrated to us a hadith about which he praised him, saying: He was a scholar, an imam in tafsir and usul. And Shaykh Abu al-Hasan 'Abd al-Ghafir ibn Isma'il mentioned in what he wrote to me: Salman ibn Nasir ibn 'Imran ibn Muhammad ibn Isma'il ibn Ishaq ibn Yazid ibn Ziyad Abu al-Qasim al-Ansari, the imam of religion, pious, ascetic, unique of his time in his field. He had knowledge of the path (tariqah) and precedence in Sufism, precise insight, reflection on transactions (mu'amala), integrity in himself, and abstemiousness in food. He was of good method, precise in insight, aware of the ways of the imams and their paths in the science of kalam (ilm al-kalam), insightful in admonitions of forms, with a limitation in his tongue's articulation. His knowledge was beyond his speech, and his meaning was more abundant than his appearance and content. And he lived the life of the pious on the conduct of the righteous predecessors (al-salaf al-salihin). He died on the morning of Monday, the 22nd of Jumada al-Akhirah of the year 512 AH.
Source pages p. 234

Commentary
This biographical entry begins with a chain of transmission: Ibn 'Asakir heard from a shaykh in Baghdad who praised al-Ansari as a scholar and imam in tafsir (Qur'anic exegesis) and usul (principles of jurisprudence). Then a longer description is quoted from 'Abd al-Ghafir, giving al-Ansari's full lineage and honorifics. The description emphasizes his piety (al-dīn), scrupulousness (al-wara‘), and asceticism (al-zuhd), calling him unique in his time. He had knowledge of the spiritual path (al-ṭarīqa) and precedence in Sufism (taṣawwuf). He possessed precise insight (naẓar daqīq) and reflection on mu'amala (spiritual dealings). He was upright in character and abstemious. His method was good, his insight precise, and he was well-versed in the ways of the imams in kalām, insightful in admonitions. However, he had a shortcoming in his tongue's expression (taqrīr lisānih); his knowledge surpassed his speech. He lived like the pious (abrār) following the salaf. He died in 512 AH.

Key Terms
التفسير (tafsīr)
الأصول (uṣūl)
التصوف (taṣawwuf)
علم الكلام (ilm al-kalām)
السلف الصالحين (al-salaf al-ṣāliḥīn)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What limitation did al-Ansari have despite his deep knowledge?
A) Weak memory
B) Lack of students
C) Shortcoming in verbal expression
D) Poor eyesight

Key Takeaway
Imam al-Ansari was a master of both rational theology and spiritual discipline, illustrating that knowledge and piety go hand in hand.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Al-Ansari's knowledge was 'beyond his speech'—he knew more than he could express. Are you more concerned with sounding knowledgeable or with truly understanding? What is one area where you can prioritize depth of understanding over outward expression starting today?
?
He combined precise insight in kalam with spiritual discipline and asceticism. Which of these two dimensions—intellectual learning or soul-purification—do you neglect? What concrete step will you take this week to restore balance?
?
He lived 'the life of the pious on the conduct of the righteous predecessors.' Think of one habit or attitude you have that clearly differs from the way of the salaf. Will you change it? What is the first small action you can take to align with their example?

Biography of Imam Abu Nasr al-Qushayri
Ibn Asakir narrates the life and scholarly career of Abu Nasr al-Qushayri.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the scholarly upbringing and achievements of Abu Nasr al-Qushayri, and how he was received in Baghdad.

Core Idea
Abu Nasr al-Qushayri embodied his father's legacy and became a leading scholar in his own right.

This lesson presents the biography of Abu Nasr al-Qushayri as recorded by Ibn Asakir. We learn about his early education under his father, his advanced studies under Imam al-Haramayn, and his remarkable reception in Baghdad. The passage highlights his mastery of various sciences and his impact on the scholarly community.

Guided Path
1
Read the biography passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once and then its translation to get familiar with the narrative.
2
Identify key figures
Note the mention of his father Abd al-Karim al-Qushayri, Imam al-Haramayn al-Juwayni, and Abu Ishaq al-Shirazi.
These are important scholars in the passage.
3
Observe the sequence of education and travels
Follow the order: early education under father, then study under Imam al-Haramayn, then Hajj, then Baghdad, then second Hajj and return.
4
Reflect on the reception and its consequences
Notice how he was accepted in Baghdad, the near fitna, and the summon by Nizam al-Mulk.
This shows his influence and the political context.

And among them is the imam, son of the imam, Abu Nasr ibn Abi al-Qasim al-Qushayri (may God have mercy on him). He wrote to me: 'Abd al-Rahim ibn 'Abd al-Karim ibn Hawazin al-Qushayri Abu Nasr, imam of imams and scholar of the community. He is the first of the children of the imam after the 'asaba al-daqaqiyya? from his children, the most resembling him in nature, until it was as if he were split from him. He raised him in the best upbringing and taught him Arabic in his youth thoroughly until he became distinguished in it and excelled in it, as well as in prose and poetry, winning the race in both. He would disseminate poetry with his pens on parchment. He attained the fullest share of the science of usul and tafsir, received directly from his father. He was given such speed in writing that he would write bundles daily routinely without great difficulty, so that he obtained various types of exact sciences and calculation (ḥisāb) needed for the science of sharia. When his father died, he moved to the circle of Imam al-Haramayn (al-Juwayni) and attended his lessons, accompanying him night and day, staying with him evening and morning until he mastered his method in the madhhab and khilaf, and he went through usul with him. Imam al-Haramayn used to rely on him and spend most of his days with him, benefiting from him in some matters of calculation in inheritance shares (farā’iḍ), estates (dūr), and bequests (waṣāyā). When he completed his study of fiqh, he prepared to travel for Hajj. When he arrived in Baghdad and held a gathering, the people of Baghdad saw his merit and perfection and witnessed his qualities, he received from them acceptance such as had not been seen for anyone before him. The elites attended his sessions, and the imams such as Imam Abu Ishaq al-Shirazi (may God have mercy on him), who was the faqih of Iraq in his time, attended his pulpit, and they agreed that they had not seen his like in depth of knowledge. He went for Hajj and when he returned, the acceptance was great, even greater than before. Partisanship for him reached such a degree that it nearly led to fitna. His gathering would seldom be free of a group of dhimmis embracing Islam. He then went out the following year returning to Hajj with complete honor and comfort in the service of the amir of the Hajj and his companions. He returned to Baghdad and the matter of acceptance remained, with fitna burgeoning nearly aflame. Then Nizam al-Mulk sent to him to summon him from Baghdad, meaning to...
Source pages p. 235

Commentary
This is a lengthy biographical entry for Abu Nasr al-Qushayri, the son of the famous Sufi scholar Abd al-Karim al-Qushayri. It begins with his name and honorific: Imam of Imams and scholar of the community. It mentions his strong resemblance to his father. He was raised well and given a thorough education in Arabic, excelling in prose and poetry. He became proficient in usul and tafsir under his father. He had remarkable speed in writing, enabling him to produce multiple sheets daily, and he mastered various exact sciences including calculation (hisab) needed for sharia, such as inheritance (fara'id). After his father's death, he studied under Imam al-Haramayn (al-Juwayni), mastering his method in fiqh and khilaf (disputed issues). He also taught al-Juwayni some calculation. After completing fiqh, he went on Hajj. In Baghdad, he gained tremendous acceptance, with even Abu Ishaq al-Shirazi attending his circle. He made a second Hajj, and his popularity grew, leading to partisanship and near fitna. Nizam al-Mulk summoned him to (presumably his court), but the text breaks off.

الأصول (uṣūl)
التفسير (tafsīr)
إمام الحرمين (Imām al-Ḥaramayn)
الخلاف (khilāf)
الفرائض (farā’iḍ)

Abu Nasr al-Qushayri was a versatile scholar whose education under his father and Imam al-Haramayn, and his warm reception in Baghdad, exemplify the ideal scholarly career in classical Islam.

?
His gatherings in Baghdad led many non-Muslims to embrace Islam. Is your own conduct and knowledge drawing people closer to the truth, or are you a barrier? Examine your intention: do you study to gain Allah's pleasure or for reputation? What will you change today so that your knowledge becomes a means of guidance for others?
?
The passage warns of fitna arising from excessive partisanship for a scholar. Are you attached to any scholar or group to the point of blind loyalty? How can you love and respect scholars without falling into division and conflict? Ask yourself: is your love for the scholar rooted in love for Allah and His Messenger, or in sectarian pride?

Abu Nasr al-Qushayri: Life and Miraculous Cure
Biography of Abu Nasr al-Qushayri with a miraculous cure story

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the life of Abu Nasr al-Qushayri, his scholarly dedication, and the significance of the miraculous cure through the key of the Kaaba.

Core Idea
Blessing from sacred objects is real, but all healing comes from Allah.

This passage from Ibn 'Asakir's Tabyin Kadhib al-Muftari presents a biographical sketch of the scholar Abu Nasr al-Qushayri, highlighting his travels, his devotion to learning, and a remarkable story of healing through the key of the Kaaba. The narrative illustrates both the reverence for sacred relics and the ultimate reliance on Divine power.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage
Read the Arabic text once without focusing on details. Then read the translation to get the overall narrative.
Pay attention to the flow of events.
2
Identify the major phases of his life
The passage covers his travels to Isfahan, Baghdad, Khurasan, Qazwin, and his return. Note the reactions of people and his scholarly activities.
3
Examine the miraculous cure story
Focus on the details: the illness, the unknown sheikh, the key of the Kaaba, and the immediate healing. Consider the theological implications.
The story illustrates baraka (blessing) from sacred objects.
4
Reflect on the lesson for Aqeedah
Think about how this narrative affirms that Allah is the ultimate healer, but He may use means like sacred relics. Avoid misunderstanding the key as having independent power.
The passage guards against the misconception that the key itself cures.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
أصبهان فاكرم مورده وبقى أهل بغداد عطاشاً إليه وإلى كلامه ، منهم من لم يفطر عن الصوم سنين بعده ومنهم من لم يحضر من بعده مجلس تذکیر قط، وأشار الصاحب عليه بالرجوع إلى خراسان ووصله بصلات سنيــة ودخل قزوين ولقى بها قبولاً تاما وحصل منهم على قريب من ألف دينار ، ولما عاد أستقبله الأئمة والصدور وكان يواظب بعد ما لقى من القبول على درس الإمام إمام الحرمين ويشتغل بزيادة التحصيل وكان أكثر صغوا في آخر أيامه إلى الرواية قلما يخلو يوم من أيامه إلا ما شاء الله عن مجلس الحديث أو مجلسين ، وتوفى عديم النظير فريد الوقت بقية أكابر الـدنـيـا ضـحـوة يوم الجمعة الثامن والعشرين من جمادى الآخرة سنة أربع عشرة وخمسمائة . ومن ظريف ما حكى من أحواله قال مرغت بمكة مرضاً شديداً مخوفا أيست فيه من الحياة فدخل على شيخ مكي لم أعرفه ولم أطلبه وبيده مفتاح الكعبة وهو من بني شيبة خزنة البيت فقال لي أفتح ففتحت فمن فأدخل المفتاح في فمي و اداره فيه ثم مسح سائر أعضائى بذلك المفتاح على لين ورفق فبرأت من علتي فكأنما أنشطت من عقال ببركة ذلك المفتاح وعافاني الله في الوقت .
He honored Isfahan with his presence, and the people of Baghdad remained thirsty for him and his speech. Among them were those who did not break their fast for years after him, and among them were those who never attended a reminder session after him. Al-Sahib indicated to him to return to Khurasan and gave him generous gifts. He entered Qazwin and received full acceptance there, obtaining nearly a thousand dinars from them. When he returned, the imams and notables received him. After the acceptance he received, he continued attending the lessons of Imam al-Haramayn and devoted himself to increasing his studies. In his later days, his inclination was mostly towards narration; hardly a day passed without one or two hadith sessions, except by God's will. He died without equal, unique of his time, the remainder of the great ones of the world, in the forenoon of Friday, the 28th of Jumada al-Akhira, 514 AH. Among the amusing stories related about him, he said: 'I fell severely and dangerously ill in Mecca, despairing of life. Then an old Meccan sheikh entered upon me whom I did not know and did not seek, and in his hand was the key of the Kaaba. He was from the Banu Shayba, the custodians of the House. He said to me: "Open your mouth," so I opened it. Then he inserted the key into my mouth and moved it around inside, then wiped all my limbs with that key gently and softly. So I recovered from my illness as if I had been untied from a fetter, by the blessing of that key, and God cured me instantly.'
Source pages p. 236

Commentary
This passage is a biographical account of Abu Nasr al-Qushayri, describing his travels, scholarly dedication, and a miraculous healing. It begins by noting how he was welcomed in Isfahan and that the people of Baghdad longed for him after he left. Some people even fasted for years after him in veneration, and others never attended any reminder session after him. Then it mentions that the vizier (al-Sahib) advised him to return to Khurasan and gave him generous gifts. He went to Qazwin where he was well received and collected nearly a thousand dinars. Upon returning, he was greeted by imams and notables. He continued attending the lessons of Imam al-Haramayn (al-Juwayni) and focused on increasing his knowledge. In his later years, he turned mostly to hadith narration, hardly missing a day without holding one or two hadith sessions. He died on Friday, 28 Jumada al-Akhira 514 AH, being unique and without equal. The narrative then shares a curious story from his life: he fell gravely ill in Mecca and despaired of life. An unknown sheikh from Banu Shayba, the custodians of the Kaaba, came with the key of the Kaaba. He instructed him to open his mouth, inserted the key, moved it around, then wiped his limbs with it. He was instantly cured, as if released from a bond, by the blessing of the key. This story illustrates the reverence for sacred objects and the belief in their baraka (blessing).

Key Terms
أبو نصر القشيري
مفتاح الكعبة
بني شيبة
إمام الحرمين
قزوين

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The key of the Kaaba has independent healing power.
Correction: The passage attributes the cure to Allah ('wa 'afani Allah'), and the key is a means of blessing (baraka), not an independent agent.

Checkpoint
What did the sheikh with the key of the Kaaba do to heal Abu Nasr al-Qushayri?
A) He recited verses over him
B) He inserted the key into his mouth and wiped his limbs
C) He gave him water from Zamzam
D) He prayed for him

Key Takeaway
Allah is the ultimate healer, and sacred objects like the key of the Kaaba can be means of blessing, but they have no independent power.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you are seriously ill, do you find yourself relying more on medical treatment and prayers, or do you truly place your ultimate hope in Allah alone? What would change if you internalized that all healing comes from Him?
?
Have you ever sought blessings from something associated with a sacred place or person? How do you guard your heart from believing that the object itself has power, rather than seeing it as a means from Allah?
?
Reflect on a time you felt utterly hopeless like Abu Nasr. In that moment, did you receive help from an unexpected source? How did you recognize Allah's hand in that help, and how can you deepen that recognition?

Al-Fayruzabadi's Witness Statement on Al-Qushayri's Orthodoxy
Al-Fayruzabadi attests to al-Qushayri's orthodoxy and urges punishing the innovators.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand al-Fayruzabadi's testimony regarding al-Qushayri's defense of orthodox Ash'ari creed and the historical context of the madrasa built to support it.

Core Idea
A witness statement confirms al-Qushayri's role in guiding Mujassima to orthodoxy and calls for punishment of remaining innovators.

In this passage, we read a formal witness statement by Ibrahim al-Fayruzabadi, a contemporary scholar. He attests that Abu Nasr al-Qushayri taught the correct beliefs of Ahl al-Sunna, refuted anthropomorphism, and succeeded in guiding many Mujassima to the truth. However, a few bitter innovators remained, slandering al-Qushayri and Imam al-Shafi'i. Al-Fayruzabadi urges the ruler to take action against them and highlights the madrasa built to uphold the madhhab.

Guided Path
1
Read the witness statement
Read the Arabic passage and its translation to get an overall sense of the testimony. Notice the formal opening and closing.
The phrase 'la yamuhu' in the translation is unclear due to OCR; it likely means something like 'with supplication for his sake'.
2
Identify al-Qushayri's role
Note how al-Fayruzabadi describes al-Qushayri's teaching: he held sessions, mentioned Allah with befitting attributes, negated tashbih, and suppressed innovators. He states that many Mujassima were guided by him.
3
Understand the conflict
See that a small group of innovators remained, driven by envy and anger, slandering al-Qushayri and al-Shafi'i and his followers. These are the ones who need to be addressed.
4
Note the call to action
Al-Fayruzabadi calls on the ruler to punish these few, warning of divine accountability if he neglects. The madrasa is presented as a blessed institution that enrages the innovators.
The madrasa likely refers to a local one built to support Ash'arism, not a specific famous madrasa.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
صورة الخطوط الأمر على ما ذكر في هذا المحضر من حال الشيخ الإمام الأوحد أبى نصر عبد الرحيم بن عبد الكريم القشيري ، أكثر الله في أئمة الدين مثله من عقد المجالس وذكر الله عز وجل بما يليق به من توحيده وصفاته ونفى التشبيه عنه ، وقمع المبتدعة من المجسمة والقدرية وغيرهم ، ولم أسمع منه غير مذهب أهل الحق من أهل السنة والجماعة ، وبه أدين الله عز وجل وإياه أعتقد وهو الذى أدركت أئمة أصحابنا عليه واهتدى به خلق كثير من المجسمة، وصاروا كلهم على مذهب أهل الحق ولم يبق من المبتدعة إلا نفر يسير فحملهم الحسد والغيظ على سبه وسب الشافعي وأئمة أصحابه ونصار مذهبه ، وهذا أمر لا يجوز الصبر عليهه ، ويتعين على المولى أعز الله نصره التنكيل بهذا النفر اليسير الذين تولوا كبر هذا الأمر وطعنوا في الشافعي وأصحابه ، لأن الله عز وجل أقدره وهو الذي برأ في هذا البلد باعزاز هذا المذهب بما بنى فيه من المدرسة التي مات كل مبتدع من المجسمة والقدرية غيظاً منها ، وبما يرتفع فيها من الأصوات بالدعاء لا يامه استجاب الله فيه صالح الأدعية ، ومتى أهمل نصرهم لم يكن له عذر عند الله عز وجل . وكتب إبراهيم بن على الفيروزآبادي
The form of the lines is that the matter is as mentioned in this record concerning the state of the unique teacher Abu Nasr Abd al-Rahim ibn Abd al-Karim al-Qushayri—may God increase in the imams of religion his like—of holding sessions and mentioning God Almighty with what befits Him of His unity and attributes, and negating anthropomorphism from Him, and suppressing the innovators from the Mujassima, Qadariyya, and others. And I have not heard from him anything other than the doctrine of the people of truth from Ahl al-Sunna wa al-Jama'a, and with it I worship God Almighty, and it is what I believe. And it is what I found the imams of our companions upon, and many people from the Mujassima were guided by him, and they all became on the doctrine of the people of truth. There remained of the innovators only a few individuals, so envy and anger drove them to insult him and insult al-Shafi'i and the imams of his companions and the supporters of his madhhab. And this is a matter that cannot be tolerated. It is incumbent upon the master—may God strengthen his victory—to punish this small group who undertook the great part of this matter and attacked al-Shafi'i and his companions, because God Almighty has empowered him, and He created in this city the exaltation of this madhhab by building in it the madrasa from which every innovator from the Mujassima and Qadariyya died of rage, and by the voices raised in it with supplication to his 'la yamuhu' [؟], God responded to it with righteous supplications. And if he neglects their support, he will have no excuse before God Almighty. Written by Ibrahim ibn Ali al-Fayruzabadi.
Source pages p. 238

Commentary
This passage is a sworn witness statement by Ibrahim al-Fayruzabadi. He confirms that Abu Nasr al-Qushayri taught the orthodox Ash'ari creed (tawhid, attributes, negation of tashbih) and suppressed innovators. He states that many Mujassima were guided through him, and only a few remain bitter. He urges the ruler to punish these few who slander al-Shafi'i and his followers. He mentions a madrasa built by the ruler that caused innovators to die of rage, and warns of divine accountability if support is neglected.

المجسمة
القدرية
المدرسة
الشيخ القشيري

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The madrasa mentioned is a specific famous madrasa like the Nizamiyya.
Correction: The passage does not specify the madrasa; it was likely built by the local ruler to support Ash'arism.

Checkpoint

A) They became more entrenched.

D) They formed a new sect.

Key Takeaway
Al-Fayruzabadi's witness statement affirms al-Qushayri's orthodoxy and the success of his efforts in guiding the Mujassima, while condemning the remainder and urging the ruler to act.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you hear about someone being guided from falsehood to truth, do you celebrate or do you feel a twinge of envy that you weren't the one credited? What does that reveal about your heart's attachment to truth versus your ego?
?
Al-Fayruzabadi publicly declared his belief and called for action against slanderers. Is there a truth you know but are too afraid to speak up about? What would it take for you to write your own witness statement?
?
The ruler was reminded that neglecting support for the truth leaves him without excuse before Allah. What authority do you have—over your family, your time, your resources—that you are neglecting to defend and promote the truth of al-Qushayri's message?

Life of Imam Ibn Asakir
review
5 min
Testimonies Praising al-Qushayri and Condemning His Detractors
Ibn Asakir records multiple testimonies praising al-Qushayri's defense of Sunni creed.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how multiple contemporary scholars testified that Imam al-Qushayri was a champion of Sunni orthodoxy against anthropomorphist innovators, and how his detractors responded with slander and cursing of Imam al-Shafi'i.

Core Idea
The testimonies prove al-Qushayri was a champion of tawhid and tanzih, opposed by envious innovators.

This passage records sworn statements from several leading scholars who observed al-Qushayri’s assemblies. They confirm that he taught correct Islamic creed, negated anthropomorphism, and that many people were guided by him. They also detail the vicious response from his opponents, who resorted to cursing Imam al-Shafi'i and his followers, prompting a call for authorities to intervene.

Guided Path
1
Read the testimonies carefully
Read the Arabic passage and its translation once to get a sense of the flow. Notice that each testimony follows a similar pattern: affirmation of al-Qushayri's activities, his teaching of tawhid and tanzih, his success in guiding people, and the envious reaction of opponents who curse al-Shafi'i.
There are five testimonies, each from a different scholar.
2
Identify the common structure
Each testimony begins with a phrase like 'The matter is as mentioned' and then adds details specific to that witness. Identify the recurring themes: tawhid, tanzih, negation of tashbih, and the charge of envy.
3
Note the specific accusation
All testimonies emphasize that the opponents cursed Imam al-Shafi'i publicly. This is the main grievance. Consider why this would be a serious issue in that context.
Cursing a leading imam was a sign of sectarian hostility.
4
Consider the historical context
These testimonies were likely submitted to the authorities to urge action against the detractors. The passage mentions the 'high council' and the need to 'cut off the source of corruption.' Reflect on the political and theological tensions of the time.
The Nizamiyya and al-Maymuniyya schools were centers of Shafi'i learning.
5
Reflect on the significance
This passage shows the intense debate against anthropomorphism and the importance of al-Qushayri's role in defending Sunni orthodoxy. It also illustrates how personal attacks on scholars were used as a weapon.
Consider how this relates to broader issues of creed and authority.

⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتب الحسين بن محمد الطبري : الأمر على ما شرح في صدر هذا المحضر . وكتب عبد الله بن سلامة الكرخي : الأمر على ما ذكر في هذا المحضر من حال الشيخ الإمام الأوحد أبي نصر عبد الرحيم بن عبد الكريم القشيرى أدام الله حراسته ، من عقد المجالس للوعظ والتذكير في المدرسة النظامية المعمورة والرباط وأطب في توحيد الله عز وجل والثناء عليه بما يستوجبه من صفات الكمال وتنزيهه عن النقائص ونفى التشبيه عنه واستوفى في الاعتقاد ما هو معتقد أهل السنة ، بأوضح الحجج وأقوى البراهين فوقع في النفوس كلامه ، ومال إليه الخلق الكثير من العامة ورجع جماعة كثيرة عن اعتقاد التجسيم والتشبيه ، واعترفت بأنها الآن بان لها الحق فحسده المبتدعة المجسمة وغيرهم فحملهم ذلك على بسط اللسان فيه غيظاً منه، وسب الشافعي رحمة الله عليه وأئمة أصحابه ومن ينصرهم ، و تظاهروا من ذلك بما لا يمكن الصبر معه ويتعين على من جعل الله إليه أمر الرعية أن يتقدم في ذلك بما يحسم مادة الفساد لأن سبب ذلك فرط غيظهم من اجتماع شمل العصابة الشافعية في الاشتغال بالعلم بعمارة المدرسة الميمونة ، وتوفرهم على الدعاء لأيام من به عزهم ولا عذر للتفريط في ذلك وكتب محمد بن أحمد الشاشي : الأمر على ما ذكر فيه . وكتب سعد الله بن محمد الخطيب : الأمر على المشروح في هذا الصدر من حال الشيخ الإمام الأوحد أبي عبد الرحيم بن عبد الكريم القشيري ، أكثر الله في أئمة أهل العلم مثله عقد المجالس ونشر العلم ووصف الله تعالى بما وصف به نفسه من توحيده وصفاته ونفى التشبيه عنه وقمع أهل البدع من المجسمة والقدرية وغيرهم ولم أسمع منه عدولاً عن مذاهب أهل الحق والسنة والدين القويم والمنهج المستقيم، الذى به يدان الله تعالى ويعبد ويعمل به ويعتقد ، فاهتدى بهديه خلق من المخالفين وصار إلي قوله ومعتقده جمع كثير إلا من شقى به من الحاسدين فأخلدوا إلى ذمه وسبه وسب أئمة الشافعيين وقدحوا في الشافعي وأصحابه وصرحوا بالطعن فيهم في الأسواق وعلى رؤوس الأشهاد ، وهذه غمة ورده لا يرجى لكشفها بعد الله تعالى إلا المجلس السامي الأجلى النظامي القوامى العادلى الرضوى ، أمتع الله الدنيا والدين ببقائه وحرس على الإسلام والمسلمين ظليل ظله ونعمائه ويفعل الله ذلك بقدرته وطوله ومشيئته . وكتب الحسين بن أحمد البغدادي : حضرت المدرسة النظامية المنصورة المعمورة أدام الله سلطان إعزازها والرباط المقدس للصوفية أجاب الله صالح أدعيتهم في المسلمين مجالس هذا الشيخ الأجل الإمام ناصر الدين ، محى الإسلام ، أبي نصر عبد الرحيم ابن الأستاذ الإمام زين الإسلام أبى القسم القشيري ، أحسن الله عن الشريعة جزاءه ، فلم أسمع منه قط إلا ما يجب على كل مكلف علمه وتصحيح العقيدة به من علم الأصول وتنزيه الحق سبحانه وتعالى ونفى التشبيه عنه واقماع الأباطيل والأضاليل وأظهار الحق والصدق حتى أسلم على يديه ببركة التوحيد والتنزيه من أنواع أهل الذمة عشرات ورجع إلى الحق وعلم الصدق من المبتدعة مئات ، وتبعه خلق غير محصور بحيث لم يستطع أحد ممن تقدم أو علماء العصر أن يشقوا غباره فى مثل ذلك فخامرهم الحسد وعداوة الجهل وحملهم على الطعن فيه عدواناً وبهتانا ثم تمادى بهم الجهل إلى اللعن الظاهر للإمام الشافعي قدس الله روحه وسائر أصحابه عجماً وعرباً وقائلو ذلك شر.
Al-Husayn ibn Muhammad al-Tabari wrote: The matter is as explained at the beginning of this document. And Abdullah ibn Salama al-Karkhi wrote: The matter is as mentioned in this document regarding the situation of the unique imam Abu Nasr Abd al-Rahim ibn Abd al-Karim al-Qushayri—may God preserve him—from his holding of assemblies for admonition and remembrance in the flourishing Nizamiyya school and the ribat, and his expertise in the unification of God Almighty and praising Him with what He deserves of attributes of perfection, and declaring Him transcendent of deficiencies, and negating anthropomorphism from Him, and he covered in creed what is the belief of Ahl al-Sunna, with the clearest proofs and strongest evidences, so his speech fell into the hearts, and many common people inclined towards him, and a large group returned from the belief in corporealism and anthropomorphism, and acknowledged that the truth had now become clear to them. So the innovators, the corporealists and others, envied him, and that led them to spread their tongue against him out of spite, and to curse al-Shafi'i—may God's mercy be upon him—and the leading imams of his companions and those who support them, and they made a display of that in a way that cannot be tolerated. It is incumbent upon the one to whom God has entrusted the affairs of the subjects to take action in that matter so as to cut off the source of corruption, because the cause of that is their extreme spite at the gathering together of the Shafi'i group in occupying themselves with knowledge in the flourishing al-Maymuniyya school, and their devoting themselves to prayer for the days of the one through whom they have honor; and there is no excuse for negligence in that. And Muhammad ibn Ahmad al-Shashi wrote: The matter is as mentioned therein. And Sa'd Allah ibn Muhammad al-Khatib wrote: The matter is as described at the beginning of this document regarding the situation of the unique imam Abu Abd al-Rahim ibn Abd al-Karim al-Qushayri—may God increase among the imams of the people of knowledge someone like him—his holding of assemblies, spreading knowledge, describing God Almighty with what He described Himself with of His tawhid and attributes, negating anthropomorphism from Him, and suppressing the people of innovation from the corporealists, Qadarites, and others. And I did not hear from him any deviation from the doctrines of the people of truth and the Sunna, the straight religion, and the upright path, by which God Almighty is worshipped and served and acted upon and believed. So many of the opponents were guided by his guidance, and a large number turned to his saying and his creed, except those who were wretched among the envious, so they persisted in defaming him and cursing him and cursing the imams of the Shafi'is and disparaged al-Shafi'i and his companions, and openly slandered them in the markets and on the heads of the crowds. This is a calamity and an affliction whose removal—after God Almighty—can only be hoped for from the most exalted, most eminent, Nizami, Qawwami, Adali, Radawi court—may God delight the world and the religion with his survival, and protect Islam and Muslims under the shadow of his shade and his favors, and God will do that by His power, bounty, and will. And al-Husayn ibn Ahmad al-Baghdadi wrote: I attended the victorious, flourishing Nizamiyya school—may God perpetuate the power of its glorification—and the holy ribat of the Sufis—may God answer their righteous prayers concerning the Muslims—the assemblies of this most venerable shaykh, the Imam Nasir al-Din, the reviver of Islam, Abu Nasr Abd al-Rahim, son of the teacher, the Imam Zayn al-Islam Abu al-Qasim al-Qushayri—may God reward him well on behalf of the Sharia. I never heard from him anything except what is obligatory for every accountable person to know and to correct his creed thereby, from the science of principles (usul) and the transcendence (tanzih) of the Truth—Glorious and Exalted is He—and the negation of anthropomorphism from Him, and the suppression of falsehoods and errors, and the manifestation of truth and honesty, until there converted at his hands, by the blessing of tawhid and tanzih, tens of the various kinds of dhimmis, and hundreds of the innovators returned to the truth and the knowledge of honesty; and countless followers followed him, such that no one from the earlier or later scholars could compete with him in that. So envy and the enmity of ignorance overwhelmed them and led them to attack him aggressively and falsely, and then ignorance drove them to open cursing of Imam al-Shafi'i—may God sanctify his soul—and all his companions, non-Arabs and Arabs, and those who say that are evil.
Source pages p. 239

Commentary
This passage is a collection of sworn testimonies (mahdars) from multiple scholars—al-Husayn ibn Muhammad al-Tabari, Abdullah ibn Salama al-Karkhi, Muhammad ibn Ahmad al-Shashi, Sa'd Allah ibn Muhammad al-Khatib, and al-Husayn ibn Ahmad al-Baghdadi—attesting to the orthodox creed and activities of Abu Nasr Abd al-Rahim al-Qushayri. Each testimony follows a similar structure: affirming that al-Qushayri held public assemblies for preaching, taught the oneness of God (tawhid) and His attributes of perfection, strictly negated anthropomorphism (tashbih) and corporealism (tajsim), and used clear proofs to establish the creed of Ahl al-Sunna. They report that many common people and even opponents turned to the truth through him, while the innovators (especially the Mujassima) were filled with envy and spite, leading them to slander al-Qushayri and also to curse Imam al-Shafi'i and his followers. The testimonies emphasize that this slander has become public and intolerable, and they call upon the ruler (the 'high council' or the sultan) to take action to stop the corruption, since the cause is the envious anger at the Shafi'i scholars gathering to study and revive the Shafi'i school at the al-Maymuniyya school. The last testimony from al-Husayn al-Baghdadi adds that al-Qushayri's efforts led to the conversion of tens of non-Muslims and the return of hundreds of innovators, and that no one could match him in this field. The passage thus serves as a historical record defending al-Qushayri and urging the authorities to suppress his detractors.

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That al-Qushayri was a controversial figure whose teachings were widely rejected.
Correction: These testimonies from multiple scholars show that he was a champion of Sunni orthodoxy, widely respected, and that his opponents were a minority driven by envy.

Checkpoint
What is the primary complaint of the scholars testifying against al-Qushayri's opponents?
A) That they abandoned prayer and fasting.
B) That they slandered al-Qushayri and cursed Imam al-Shafi'i publicly.
C) That they denied the existence of God.
D) That they refused to attend the Nizamiyya school.

Key Takeaway
The testimonies collected by Ibn Asakir demonstrate that al-Qushayri was uniformly regarded by contemporary scholars as a defender of Sunni orthodoxy, while his opponents are portrayed as envious innovators who resorted to cursing Imam al-Shafi'i.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you see someone defending the truth and being attacked by others, does your heart lean toward defending them or toward joining the critics? What does that reveal about your own relationship with truth and justice?
?
Envy (hasad) is described as the driving force behind slandering al-Qushayri. Where in your life has envy caused you to speak ill of someone who is doing good? What step will you take this week to purify your heart from this disease?
?
The testimonies called on the ruler to act against the slanderers. If you have influence in any sphere (family, workplace, community), are you using it to support truth and silence falsehood, or are you remaining silent out of fear or indifference?

Life of Imam Ibn Asakir
beginner

Testimonies of Al-Shashi and Al-Khatib on Al-Qushayri's Orthodoxy
First two testimonies affirm al-Qushayri's orthodoxy.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how two scholars, Muhammad al-Shashi and Sa'd Allah al-Khatib, publicly affirmed Abd al-Rahim al-Qushayri's commitment to Sunni doctrine and his role in combating anthropomorphism.

Core Idea
Al-Qushayri's orthodoxy was certified by multiple Shafi'i scholars.

The passage opens with a description of the Shafi'i community's engagement in knowledge and then presents the first two testimonies. Al-Shashi's brief note confirms victory, while al-Khatib provides a detailed account of al-Qushayri's teaching of tawhid, negation of anthropomorphism, and his refutation of innovators. This lesson focuses on these early endorsements.

Guided Path
1
Read the opening context
Read the first line describing the gathering of the Shafi'i group devoted to knowledge. Understand the setting of these testimonies.
This context highlights the collective effort of the Shafi'i scholars.
2
Examine al-Shashi's brief testimony
Muhammad ibn Ahmad al-Shashi writes a short statement: 'Victory comes from the matter as mentioned in it.' Note how this is a concise confirmation.
The brevity may indicate that the details were already known.
3
Analyze al-Khatib's detailed testimony
Sa'd Allah al-Khatib provides a fuller account. Identify the key points: al-Qushayri held sessions, described Allah as He described Himself, negated anthropomorphism, and suppressed innovators.
This testimony explicitly mentions the Mujassima and Qadariyya as the opponents.
4
Identify the call for ruler intervention
Al-Khatib ends by expressing hope for relief from the Nizami council, showing reliance on political authority to resolve the conflict.
5
Reflect on the significance
Consider why multiple testimonies were needed and what this says about the theological controversies of the time.
The testimonies serve as legal evidence of orthodoxy.
