من اجتماع شمل العصابة الشافعية في الاشتغال بالعلم بعمارة المدرسة الميمونة ، وتوفرهم على الدعاء لأيام من به عزهم ولا عذر للتفريط في ذلك وكتب محمد بن أحمد الشاشي : 
نصر من الأمر على ما ذكر فيه . وكتب سعد الله بن محمد الخاطب : الأمر على المشروح في هذا الصدر من حال الشيخ الإمام الأوحد أبي عبد الرحيم بن عبد الكريم القشيري ، أكثر الله في أئمة أهل العلم مثله عقد المجالس ونشر العلم ووصف الله تعالى بما وصف به نفسه من توحيده وصفاته ونفى التشبيه عنه وقمع أهل البدع من المجسمة والقدرية وغيرهم ولم أسمع منه عدولاً عن مذاهب أهل الحق والسنة والدين القويم والمنهج المستقيم، الذى به يدان الله تعالى ويعبد ويعمل به ويعتقد ، فاهتدى بهديه خلق من المخالفين وصار إلي قوله ومـعـتـقـده جمع كثير إلا من شقى به من الحاسدين فأخلدوا إلى ذمه وسبه وسب أئمة الشافعيين وقدحوا في الشافعي وأصحابه وصرحوا بالطعن فيهم في الأسواق وعلى رؤوس الأشهاد ، وهذه غمة ورده لا يرجى لكشفها بعد الله تعالى إلا المجلس السامي الأجلى النظامي القوامى العادلى الرضوى ، أمتع الله الدنيا والدين ببقائه وحرس على الإسلام والمسلمين ظليل ظله ونعمائه ويفعل الله ذلك بقدرته وطوله ومشيئته . وكتب الحسين بن أحمد البغدادي : 
حضرت المدرسة النظامية المنصورة المعمورة أدام الله سلطان إعزازها والرباط المقدس للصوفية أجاب الله صالح أدعيتهم في المسلمين مجالس هذا الشيخ الأجل الإمام ناصر الدين ، محى الإسلام ، أبي نصر عبد الرحيم ابن الأستاذ الإمام زين الإسلام أبى القسم القشيري ، أحسن الله عن الشريعة جزاءه ، فلم أسمع منه قط إلا ما يجب على كل مكلف علمه وتصحيح العقيدة به من علم الأصول وتنزيه الحق سبحانه وتعالى ونفى التشبيه عنه واقماع الأباطيل والأضاليل وأظهار الحق والصدق حتى أسلم على يديه ببركة التوحيد والتنزيه من أنواع أهل الذمة عشرات ورجع إلى الحق وعلم الصدق من المبتدعة مئات ، وتبعه خلق غير محصور بحيث لم يستطع أحد ممن تقدم أو علماء العصر أن يشقوا غباره فى مثل ذلك فخامرهم الحسد وعداوة الجهل وحملهم على الطعن فيه عدواناً وبهتانا ثم تمادى بهم الجهل إلى اللعن الظاهر للإمام الشافعي قدس الله روحه وسائر أصحابه عجماً وعرباً وقائلو ذلك شر ذمة من ناشية أغبياء المجسمة وطائفة من أرذال الحشوية استغنوا من الإسلام بالأسم ومن العلم بالرسم ، وتبعهم سوقة لانسب لهم ولا حسب ، وتظاهرت هذه اللعنة منهم في الأسواق ولم يستحسن أحد من أصحابه كثرهم الله دفع السفاهة بالسفاهة والسيئة بالسيئة ، ويجب على الناظر في أمور المسلمين من الذى قد انتشر فى المشارق والمغارب علمه وعدله ، وأمره ونهيه الذي لطاعته نبأت صدور الأولياء والأعداء ، رغبة ورهبة نصرته ومد ضبعيه والشد على يديه ، وتقديم كلمته العليا وتدحيض كلمة أعدائه السفلى فالصبر في الصدمة الأولى وهذه الصدمة التي كانت قلوب أصحاب الشافعى كثرهم الله وغرة وغلة شغله بها منذ سنين فانقشع ذلك وانكشف في هذه الأيام المؤيدة المنصورة المؤبدة النظامية القوامية العالمية العادلية نصرها الله وأعلاها وقد وقف تمامه على الأمر الماضى المنصور منه فإن في شعبة من شعب عنايته ونصرته وكلمته للدين الذى مد أطراره كفاية وبلاغا ، وعلى الغارس تعهد غراسه فضلاً وتعصباً في كل وقت. وكتب عزيزى بن عبد الملك في التاريخ حامداً الله ومصـلـيـا علـى مـحـمـد النبى وعلى آله وصـحـبـه وسـلـم وشــرف وكرم (۱).
From the gathering of the Shafi'i group engaging in knowledge by building the blessed school, and their devoting themselves to supplication for the days through which their honor comes, and there is no excuse for negligence in that. And Muhammad ibn Ahmad al-Shashi wrote: Victory comes from the matter as mentioned in it. And Sa'd Allah ibn Muhammad al-Khatib wrote: The matter is as explained in this introduction concerning the situation of the unique shaykh and imam Abu 'Abd al-Rahim ibn 'Abd al-Karim al-Qushayri—may Allah increase among the imams of the people of knowledge the like of him. He held sessions, spread knowledge, described Allah Almighty as He described Himself regarding His tawhid and attributes, negated anthropomorphism from Him, and suppressed the people of innovation—the Mujassima, Qadariyya, and others. I never heard from him any deviation from the doctrines of the people of truth, the Sunna, the upright religion, and the straight path, by which Allah is worshipped, served, and believed. Many of the opponents were guided by his guidance, and a great multitude adopted his words and creed, except for those who were wretched through him among the envious. They clung to blaming and insulting him, insulting the imams of the Shafi'is, attacking al-Shafi'i and his companions, and declaring their criticism openly in the markets and in public. This is a grief and distress whose removal is hoped for, after Allah Almighty, only through the most elevated, most glorious, Nizami, Qawami, 'Adali, Radawi council—may Allah give enjoyment to the world and religion through its continuance, and protect Islam and Muslims under the shadow of its shade and blessings. Allah will do that by His power, bounty, and will. And al-Husayn ibn Ahmad al-Baghdadi wrote: I attended the Nizamiyya school—the victorious, populated—may Allah perpetuate the sultan of its honor—and the sacred ribat for the Sufis—may Allah answer their righteous supplications among the Muslims—the sessions of this great shaykh, the imam, Nasir al-Din, reviver of Islam, Abu Nasr 'Abd al-Rahim, son of the master imam Zayn al-Islam Abi al-Qasim al-Qushayri—may Allah reward him well on behalf of the Shari'a. I never heard from him anything except what is obligatory for every responsible person to know and to correct creed through: the science of principles, transcending the Truth, glorifying Him, negating anthropomorphism from Him, refuting falsehoods and misguidances, and manifesting truth and sincerity. Eventually, through his blessed efforts of tawhid and transcendence, dozens of the people of dhimma converted to Islam, hundreds of innovators returned to truth and the knowledge of sincerity, and countless people followed him, so much so that no one among those who came before or the scholars of the age could reach his level in such matters. Envy and the enmity of ignorance overcame them and drove them to attack him unjustly and slanderously. Then ignorance extended them to open curse of Imam al-Shafi'i—may Allah sanctify his soul—and all his companions, non-Arabs and Arabs. Those who say that are the worst dhimma, from the foolish offspring of the Mujassima, a group of the vile Hashwiyya, who sufficed with the name of Islam and the form of knowledge. They were followed by commoners with no lineage or status. This curse spread among them in the markets, and none of his companions—may Allah increase them—approved repelling folly with folly or evil with evil. It is incumbent upon the one who oversees the affairs of Muslims—the one whose knowledge and justice have spread in the East and West, whose command and prohibition have made the hearts of saints and enemies submit to his obedience, in hope and fear—to support him, extend his arms, strengthen his hands, elevate his word, and debase the word of his enemies. Patience in the first shock—and this shock had troubled the hearts of al-Shafi'i's companions—may Allah increase them—with grief and anguish, occupying them for years. Then that cleared and was revealed in these days—the supported, victorious, eternal Nizami, Qawami, 'Alami, 'Adali—may Allah support and exalt it. Its completion depends on the passed, victorious command, for in a branch of his care, support, and word for the religion, which has extended its outskirts, is sufficient attainment. And upon the planter is the care of his planting, as favor and zeal at all times. And 'Azizi ibn 'Abd al-Malik wrote in the record, praising Allah, blessing and greeting Muhammad the Prophet, his family, and his companions, and honoring and magnifying (1).
Source pages p. 240

Commentary
This passage is a collection of three written testimonies from prominent Shafi'i scholars defending Shaykh Abd al-Rahim al-Qushayri against his detractors. The first testimony by Muhammad ibn Ahmad al-Shashi is brief, stating only that victory comes from Allah regarding what was mentioned. The second, by Sa'd Allah ibn Muhammad al-Khatib, elaborates on al-Qushayri's activities: he held scholarly sessions, taught the correct description of Allah (tawhid and attributes), negated anthropomorphism, and refuted innovators like the Mujassima (anthropomorphists) and Qadariyya. The witness affirms that he never heard any deviation from Sunni doctrine. He notes that many opponents were guided, but the envious resorted to slandering al-Qushayri and the Shafi'i imams, even attacking al-Shafi'i publicly. The witness calls for the ruler's intervention to remove this fitna. The third testimony, by al-Husayn ibn Ahmad al-Baghdadi, is more detailed. He attended al-Qushayri's sessions at the Nizamiyya school and the Sufi ribat, and testifies that al-Qushayri taught only what is obligatory for every Muslim—namely, the science of usul al-din, affirming Allah's transcendence, negating anthropomorphism, refuting falsehood, and manifesting truth. As a result, dozens of dhimmis converted to Islam and hundreds of innovators returned to the truth. Envy and ignorance led people to attack him and even curse Imam al-Shafi'i. The witness describes the opponents as ignorant Mujassima and vile Hashwiyya who have only the name of Islam and the form of knowledge, followed by commoners. He urges the ruler to support al-Qushayri, as the situation had troubled the Shafi'is for years but is now clearing due to the ruler's justice. The passage concludes with a brief note from 'Azizi ibn 'Abd al-Malik writing the record.

B) The divine attributes

Key Takeaway
The testimonies of al-Shashi and al-Khatib provide early written evidence of al-Qushayri's orthodoxy and the conflict with anthropomorphists.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you see a righteous scholar being slandered publicly, as al-Qushayri was, do you have the courage to defend the truth like al-Khatib did, even if it means facing the same insults? What holds you back?
?
Al-Khatib described al-Qushayri as 'unique' and prayed for more like him. Is there a scholar in your life whom you admire so deeply that you would testify to their orthodoxy despite opposition? How can you support them?
?
The testimony says the envious slandered al-Qushayri and even attacked Imam al-Shafi'i. Have you ever found yourself envying someone's religious knowledge or status? How can you turn that envy into sincere admiration and supplication?

Life of Imam Ibn Asakir
beginner

Al-Husayn al-Baghdadi's Testimony and the Appeal for Justice
Third testimony details al-Qushayri's teaching impact and calls for ruler support.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the detailed account of al-Qushayri's teaching impact provided by al-Husayn al-Baghdadi and the call for the ruler's support against his detractors.

Core Idea
Al-Qushayri's teaching led to mass conversions and exposed the envy of anthropomorphists.

The third testimony, by al-Husayn al-Baghdadi, is the most detailed. He describes al-Qushayri's sessions at the Nizamiyya school and the Sufi ribat, his focus on tawhid and transcendence, and the remarkable results: dozens of dhimmis converted and hundreds of innovators returned. The passage then condemns those who cursed al-Shafi'i and calls upon the ruler to intervene.

Guided Path
1
Attend the sessions of al-Qushayri
Al-Husayn describes attending al-Qushayri's sessions at the Nizamiyya school and the Sufi ribat. Picture the setting where these teachings took place.
The Nizamiyya was a prominent institution founded by Nizam al-Mulk.
2
Note the content of his teaching
Identify what al-Qushayri taught: the science of principles, tawhid, transcendence (tanzih), negation of anthropomorphism, and refutation of falsehood.
These are the core topics of Sunni creed.
3
Observe the impact: conversions and returns
Al-Husayn reports that dozens of dhimmis converted to Islam and hundreds of innovators returned to the truth as a result of al-Qushayri's efforts. This shows the practical effect of his teaching.
This highlights the success of his da'wa.
4
Understand the opposition: envy and cursing
Envy and ignorance drove opponents to attack al-Qushayri and even curse Imam al-Shafi'i. Al-Husayn describes them as foolish Mujassima and vile Hashwiyya.
The Hashwiyya were considered a group of ignorant literalists.
5
Heed the call for ruler's support
The testimony ends with a plea for the ruler to support al-Qushayri and suppress the fitna, emphasizing that the situation had troubled the Shafi'is for years but is now clearing due to the ruler's justice.

من اجتماع شمل العصابة الشافعية في الاشتغال بالعلم بعمارة المدرسة الميمونة ، وتوفرهم على الدعاء لأيام من به عزهم ولا عذر للتفريط في ذلك وكتب محمد بن أحمد الشاشي : 
نصر من الأمر على ما ذكر فيه . وكتب سعد الله بن محمد الخاطب : الأمر على المشروح في هذا الصدر من حال الشيخ الإمام الأوحد أبي عبد الرحيم بن عبد الكريم القشيري ، أكثر الله في أئمة أهل العلم مثله عقد المجالس ونشر العلم ووصف الله تعالى بما وصف به نفسه من توحيده وصفاته ونفى التشبيه عنه وقمع أهل البدع من المجسمة والقدرية وغيرهم ولم أسمع منه عدولاً عن مذاهب أهل الحق والسنة والدين القويم والمنهج المستقيم، الذى به يدان الله تعالى ويعبد ويعمل به ويعتقد ، فاهتدى بهديه خلق من المخالفين وصار إلي قوله ومـعـتـقـده جمع كثير إلا من شقى به من الحاسدين فأخلدوا إلى ذمه وسبه وسب أئمة الشافعيين وقدحوا في الشافعي وأصحابه وصرحوا بالطعن فيهم في الأسواق وعلى رؤوس الأشهاد ، وهذه غمة ورده لا يرجى لكشفها بعد الله تعالى إلا المجلس السامي الأجلى النظامي القوامى العادلى الرضوى ، أمتع الله الدنيا والدين ببقائه وحرس على الإسلام والمسلمين ظليل ظله ونعمائه ويفعل الله ذلك بقدرته وطوله ومشيئته . وكتب الحسين بن أحمد البغدادي : 
حضرت المدرسة النظامية المنصورة المعمورة أدام الله سلطان إعزازها والرباط المقدس للصوفية أجاب الله صالح أدعيتهم في المسلمين مجالس هذا الشيخ الأجل الإمام ناصر الدين ، محى الإسلام ، أبي نصر عبد الرحيم ابن الأستاذ الإمام زين الإسلام أبى القسم القشيري ، أحسن الله عن الشريعة جزاءه ، فلم أسمع منه قط إلا ما يجب على كل مكلف علمه وتصحيح العقيدة به من علم الأصول وتنزيه الحق سبحانه وتعالى ونفى التشبيه عنه واقماع الأباطيل والأضاليل وأظهار الحق والصدق حتى أسلم على يديه ببركة التوحيد والتنزيه من أنواع أهل الذمة عشرات ورجع إلى الحق وعلم الصدق من المبتدعة مئات ، وتبعه خلق غير محصور بحيث لم يستطع أحد ممن تقدم أو علماء العصر أن يشقوا غباره فى مثل ذلك فخامرهم الحسد وعداوة الجهل وحملهم على الطعن فيه عدواناً وبهتانا ثم تمادى بهم الجهل إلى اللعن الظاهر للإمام الشافعي قدس الله روحه وسائر أصحابه عجماً وعرباً وقائلو ذلك شر ذمة من ناشية أغبياء المجسمة وطائفة من أرذال الحشوية استغنوا من الإسلام بالأسم ومن العلم بالرسم ، وتبعهم سوقة لانسب لهم ولا حسب ، وتظاهرت هذه اللعنة منهم في الأسواق ولم يستحسن أحد من أصحابه كثرهم الله دفع السفاهة بالسفاهة والسيئة بالسيئة ، ويجب على الناظر في أمور المسلمين من الذى قد انتشر فى المشارق والمغارب علمه وعدله ، وأمره ونهيه الذي لطاعته نبأت صدور الأولياء والأعداء ، رغبة ورهبة نصرته ومد ضبعيه والشد على يديه ، وتقديم كلمته العليا وتدحيض كلمة أعدائه السفلى فالصبر في الصدمة الأولى وهذه الصدمة التي كانت قلوب أصحاب الشافعى كثرهم الله وغرة وغلة شغله بها منذ سنين فانقشع ذلك وانكشف في هذه الأيام المؤيدة المنصورة المؤبدة النظامية القوامية العالمية العادلية نصرها الله وأعلاها وقد وقف تمامه على الأمر الماضى المنصور منه فإن في شعبة من شعب عنايته ونصرته وكلمته للدين الذى مد أطراره كفاية وبلاغا ، وعلى الغارس تعهد غراسه فضلاً وتعصباً في كل وقت. وكتب عزيزى بن عبد الملك في التاريخ حامداً الله ومصـلـيـا علـى مـحـمـد النبى وعلى آله وصـحـبـه وسـلـم وشــرف وكرم (۱).
From the gathering of the Shafi'i group engaging in knowledge by building the blessed school, and their devoting themselves to supplication for the days through which their honor comes, and there is no excuse for negligence in that. And Muhammad ibn Ahmad al-Shashi wrote: Victory comes from the matter as mentioned in it. And Sa'd Allah ibn Muhammad al-Khatib wrote: The matter is as explained in this introduction concerning the situation of the unique shaykh and imam Abu 'Abd al-Rahim ibn 'Abd al-Karim al-Qushayri—may Allah increase among the imams of the people of knowledge the like of him. He held sessions, spread knowledge, described Allah Almighty as He described Himself regarding His tawhid and attributes, negated anthropomorphism from Him, and suppressed the people of innovation—the Mujassima, Qadariyya, and others. I never heard from him any deviation from the doctrines of the people of truth, the Sunna, the upright religion, and the straight path, by which Allah is worshipped, served, and believed. Many of the opponents were guided by his guidance, and a great multitude adopted his words and creed, except for those who were wretched through him among the envious. They clung to blaming and insulting him, insulting the imams of the Shafi'is, attacking al-Shafi'i and his companions, and declaring their criticism openly in the markets and in public. This is a grief and distress whose removal is hoped for, after Allah Almighty, only through the most elevated, most glorious, Nizami, Qawami, 'Adali, Radawi council—may Allah give enjoyment to the world and religion through its continuance, and protect Islam and Muslims under the shadow of its shade and blessings. Allah will do that by His power, bounty, and will. And al-Husayn ibn Ahmad al-Baghdadi wrote: I attended the Nizamiyya school—the victorious, populated—may Allah perpetuate the sultan of its honor—and the sacred ribat for the Sufis—may Allah answer their righteous supplications among the Muslims—the sessions of this great shaykh, the imam, Nasir al-Din, reviver of Islam, Abu Nasr 'Abd al-Rahim, son of the master imam Zayn al-Islam Abi al-Qasim al-Qushayri—may Allah reward him well on behalf of the Shari'a. I never heard from him anything except what is obligatory for every responsible person to know and to correct creed through: the science of principles, transcending the Truth, glorifying Him, negating anthropomorphism from Him, refuting falsehoods and misguidances, and manifesting truth and sincerity. Eventually, through his blessed efforts of tawhid and transcendence, dozens of the people of dhimma converted to Islam, hundreds of innovators returned to truth and the knowledge of sincerity, and countless people followed him, so much so that no one among those who came before or the scholars of the age could reach his level in such matters. Envy and the enmity of ignorance overcame them and drove them to attack him unjustly and slanderously. Then ignorance extended them to open curse of Imam al-Shafi'i—may Allah sanctify his soul—and all his companions, non-Arabs and Arabs. Those who say that are the worst dhimma, from the foolish offspring of the Mujassima, a group of the vile Hashwiyya, who sufficed with the name of Islam and the form of knowledge. They were followed by commoners with no lineage or status. This curse spread among them in the markets, and none of his companions—may Allah increase them—approved repelling folly with folly or evil with evil. It is incumbent upon the one who oversees the affairs of Muslims—the one whose knowledge and justice have spread in the East and West, whose command and prohibition have made the hearts of saints and enemies submit to his obedience, in hope and fear—to support him, extend his arms, strengthen his hands, elevate his word, and debase the word of his enemies. Patience in the first shock—and this shock had troubled the hearts of al-Shafi'i's companions—may Allah increase them—with grief and anguish, occupying them for years. Then that cleared and was revealed in these days—the supported, victorious, eternal Nizami, Qawami, 'Alami, 'Adali—may Allah support and exalt it. Its completion depends on the passed, victorious command, for in a branch of his care, support, and word for the religion, which has extended its outskirts, is sufficient attainment. And upon the planter is the care of his planting, as favor and zeal at all times. And 'Azizi ibn 'Abd al-Malik wrote in the record, praising Allah, blessing and greeting Muhammad the Prophet, his family, and his companions, and honoring and magnifying (1).

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?

?

Have you ever been satisfied with just a label or a ritual, while your heart remained ignorant of the true meanings of tawhid? Life of Imam Ibn Asakir
beginner
8 min
The Five Shafi'i Signatories and Their Credentials
Ibn 'Asakir enumerates the five Shafi'i imams who signed the testimonial document.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the scholarly credentials of the five Shafi'i imams who signed the testimonial document, as recorded by Ibn 'Asakir, and the significance of their inter-madhhab respect.

Core Idea
The signatories' biographies prove their authority and the unity of Ahl al-Sunna.

This passage from Ibn 'Asakir's Tabyin Kadhib al-Muftari introduces the five Shafi'i imams whose signatures authenticate the testimonies against the anthropomorphists. By exploring their lives, we see not only their individual excellence but also the respect between schools, as when the Hanbali Ibn 'Aqil washed the body of Abu Ishaq al-Shirazi.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and identify each scholar
Read the Arabic and translation once to get the names and key facts about each of the five imams.
Notice that each scholar is introduced with 'وأما' and given a brief biography.
2
Notice the inter-madhhab connection
Observe that the Hanbali scholar Ibn 'Aqil washed the body of the Shafi'i Abu Ishaq al-Shirazi, highlighting mutual respect despite theological differences.
This counters the misconception of perpetual hostility between schools.
3
Consider the role of these scholars as witnesses
Think about why Ibn 'Asakir includes these biographies: to establish the credibility and authority of the signatories, ensuring the testimonies are trustworthy.
Their scholarly status and widespread recognition bolster the document's strength.
4
Reflect on the broader lesson
Consider how scholarly authority is built on knowledge, piety, and recognition by peers, and how this passage exemplifies the traditional method of authenticating historical reports through reliable chains.
This is a key feature of Sunni historiography and 'ilm al-rijal.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(۱) وأصحاب الخطوط فى هذا المحضر هم كبار أئمة المذهب الشافعي ببغداد في ذلك العهد أما إبراهيم بن على الفيروز اباذى فهو إمام الأئمة أبو إسحق الشيرازي صاحب التنبيه والمهذب والنكت واللمع والتبصرة والملخص والمعونة والاشارة وطبقات الفقهاء وغيرها في الفقه والجدل والخلاف والاصلين والتراجم ، ولا يجهل جلالة قدر هذا الإمام في العلم والورع إلا من لا يعبأ الله به وقد اعترف بامامته علماء الفرق وشهرته تغنى عن كل اطراء وتوفى سنة ست وسبعين وأربعمائة عن ثلاث وثمانين سنة وتولى غسله الإمام المشهور أبو الوفاء بن عقيل الحنبلي . وأما الحسين بن محمد الطبري فهو الإمام البارع الحسين بن محمد بن على الطبري جد الطبريين بالحجاز ، من أنجب أصحاب الإمام أبي إسحق الشيرازي ، جرت بينه وبين الحنابلة القائلين بالحرف والصوت خطوب ، درس بالنظامية ببغداد والف العدة شرح الإبانة وغيرها ، توفى في حدود سنة خمس وتسعين وأربعمائة ، وأما محمد بن أحمد الشاشي فهو الإمام حافظ المذهب أبو بكر الشاشي مصنف المستظهرى ومؤلف الشافعى شرح الشامل ، صيته الذائع يغنينا عن التبسط في ترجمته وكان معيدا لدرس أبى إسحق الشيرازي ، توفى سنة سبع وخمسمائة عن ثمان وسبعين سنة ودفن في قبر شيخه أبي إسحق . وأما الحسين بن أحمد البغدادي فهو الإمام ، الكبير أبو عبد الله بن البقال الفقيه البارع النظار من أصحاب القاضي أبي الطيب وممن ولى القضاء بحريم دار الخلافة ، توفى سنة سبع وسبعين وأربعمائة عن ست وسبعين سنة . وأما تزيزى بن عبد الملك شيذله فهو الإمام أبو المعالى الجيلى مؤلف البرهان - من أقدم ما ألف
(1) The owners of the signatures in this document are the great imams of the Shafi'i school in Baghdad in that era. As for Ibrahim ibn 'Ali al-Firuzabadi, he is the imam of imams Abu Ishaq al-Shirazi, author of al-Tanbih, al-Muhadhdhab, al-Nukat, al-Luma', al-Tabsira, al-Mulakhkhas, al-Ma'una, al-Ishara, and Tabaqat al-Fuqaha' and other works in fiqh, dialectics, disagreement, the two principles, and biographies. No one ignores the majesty of this imam in knowledge and piety except one whom Allah disregards. The scholars of all sects acknowledged his imamate, and his fame suffices for all praise. He died in the year 476 AH at the age of eighty-three years, and his washing was undertaken by the famous imam Abu al-Wafa' ibn 'Aqil al-Hanbali. As for al-Husayn ibn Muhammad al-Tabari, he is the distinguished imam al-Husayn ibn Muhammad ibn 'Ali al-Tabari, the grandfather of the Tabaris in the Hijaz, from the most gifted companions of Imam Abu Ishaq al-Shirazi. Between him and the Hanbalis who affirm letter and sound there were incidents. He taught at the Nizamiyya in Baghdad and authored several works, including the commentary on al-Ibana and others. He died around the year 495 AH. As for Muhammad ibn Ahmad al-Shashi, he is the imam, the preserver of the school, Abu Bakr al-Shashi, author of al-Mustazhiri and the Shafi'i commentary on al-Shamil. His widespread fame renders us unnecessary to elaborate his biography. He was a repeater (mu'id) of Abu Ishaq al-Shirazi's lessons. He died in the year 507 AH at the age of seventy-eight years and was buried in the grave of his shaykh Abu Ishaq. As for al-Husayn ibn Ahmad al-Baghdadi, he is the great imam Abu 'Abd Allah ibn al-Baqqal, the brilliant jurist and dialectician, from the companions of Qadi Abu al-Tayyib, and among those who held judgeship in the sanctuary of the caliphal palace. He died in the year 477 AH at the age of seventy-six years. As for 'Azizi ibn 'Abd al-Malik Shidhla, he is the imam Abu al-Ma'ali al-Jili, author of al-Burhan—among the earliest authored works.
Source pages p. 241

Commentary
This passage provides biographical notes on each of the signatories of the testimonial document. It begins by stating that the signatories were the great imams of the Shafi'i school in Baghdad at that time. The first is Ibrahim ibn 'Ali al-Firuzabadi, who is the famous Abu Ishaq al-Shirazi, a leading Shafi'i jurist and author of many foundational works in fiqh, usul al-fiqh, and other disciplines. His scholarly stature is universally acknowledged. He died in 476 AH at age 83, and his funeral bath was performed by the prominent Hanbali scholar Abu al-Wafa' ibn 'Aqil—a detail highlighting mutual respect between schools. The second is al-Husayn ibn Muhammad al-Tabari, a gifted student of al-Shirazi and ancestor of the Tabari family in the Hijaz. He had conflicts with the Hanbalis who affirm letter and sound (i.e., anthropomorphists). He taught at the Nizamiyya and authored works, including a commentary on al-Ibana. He died around 495 AH. The third is Muhammad ibn Ahmad al-Shashi, Abu Bakr al-Shashi, a renowned Shafi'i hadith memorizer and author of al-Mustazhiri and a commentary on al-Shamil. He was a repeater (mu'id) of al-Shirazi's lessons. He died in 507 AH at age 78 and was buried beside his teacher. The fourth is al-Husayn ibn Ahmad al-Baghdadi, known as Ibn al-Baqqal, a brilliant jurist and dialectician, a companion of Qadi Abu al-Tayyib, and a judge in the caliphal palace. He died in 477 AH at age 76. The fifth is 'Azizi ibn 'Abd al-Malik Shidhla, who is Abu al-Ma'ali al-Jili, author of al-Burhan, one of the earliest works. These biographical notes establish the authority and credibility of the witnesses.

Key Terms
أبو إسحق الشيرازي
أبو الوفاء بن عقيل
الحنابلة
المدرسة النظامية
أبو بكر الشاشي

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The Hanbali school uniformly opposed the Shafi'is and no mutual respect existed.
Correction: The washing of al-Shirazi by Ibn 'Aqil demonstrates inter-madhhab respect and cooperation, despite theological differences on specific issues.

Checkpoint

A) Ibrahim al-Firuzabadi

Key Takeaway
The biographies of these five Shafi'i imams authenticate the testimonial document and illustrate the high regard between schools.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
The passage highlights that Imam al-Shirazi's fame was so great that it sufficed for all praise. In an age of anonymous online learning, how many of the scholars you follow do you truly know their biography and works? Will you make it a habit to learn the names and lives of the scholars whose knowledge you consume?
?
Ibn 'Aqil al-Hanbali washed the body of al-Shirazi despite their school differences. Is there any Sunni scholar from a different madhhab or tradition that you hold a grudge against? What concrete step will you take to purify your heart and show them respect, even if you disagree?
?
These imams authored numerous books and taught at prestigious institutions. You also have a platform—your family, your workplace, your social circle. What legacy of knowledge are you actively building today? If you were to die this week, what would be your contribution to the preservation of the Sunnah?

Life of Imam Ibn Asakir
beginner
8 min
The Credibility of the Signatories: Biographies of Shafi'i Imams
Ibn Asakir enumerates biographies of five Shafi'i signatories.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Ibn Asakir uses detailed biographies of respected Shafi'i scholars to establish the credibility and authority of the signatories of the petition.

Core Idea
A signatory's biography is a testimony to their reliability.

In this passage, Ibn Asakir lists the names of the Shafi'i imams who signed the document. But he does not just list names; he provides mini-biographies that highlight their scholarship, works, and positions. This is a deliberate rhetorical move to show that the signatories are not ordinary people but the leading authorities of the school, whose agreement carries weight. As you read, notice how each description reinforces their stature.

Guided Path
1
Read the opening sentence
Start by reading the first sentence: 'The signatories of this document are the great imams of the Shafi'i school in Baghdad at that time.' This sets the tone: these are not random people but the leading scholars.
2
Examine Abu Ishaq al-Shirazi's biography
Notice the lengthy description of his works and the honorific 'Imam of Imams.' This establishes him as a towering figure whose endorsement is weighty.
He is the first and most detailed, showing his preeminence.
3
Note the theological conflict in al-Tabari's entry
Al-Tabari had conflicts with Hanbalis who affirm 'letter and sound' (anthropomorphists). This clue links the petition to defending orthodox theology against anthropomorphism.
4
See how al-Shashi's fame is invoked
For al-Shashi, Ibn Asakir says 'his widespread fame suffices us from elaborating.' This assumes the reader already knows his stature, reinforcing the group's credibility.
5
Gather the overall message
Each biography contributes to a cumulative argument: these are scholars of immense knowledge and piety, so their collective signature carries authority for the document's claims.
The names are not just a list—they are evidence.

وأصحاب الخطوط فى هذا المحضر هم كبار أئمة المذهب الشافعي ببغداد في ذلك العهد أما إبراهيم بن على الفيروز اباذى فهو إمام الأئمة أبو إسحق الشيرازي صاحب التنبيه والمهذب والنكت واللمع والتبصرة والملخص والمعونة والاشارة وطبقات الفقهاء وغيرها في الفقه والجدل والخلاف والاصلين والتراجم ، ولا يجهل جلالة قدر هذا الإمام في العلم والورع إلا من لا يعبأ الله به وقد اعترف بامامته علماء الفرق وشهرته تغنى عن كل اطراء وتوفى سنة ست وسبعين وأربعمائة عن ثلاث وثمانين سنة وتولى غسله الإمام المشهور أبو الوفاء بن عقيل الحنبلي . وأما الحسين بن محمد الطبري فهو الإمام البارع الحسين بن محمد بن على الطبري جد الطبريين بالحجاز ، من أنجب أصحاب الإمام أبي إسحق الشيرازي ، جرت بينه وبين الحنابلة القائلين بالحرف والصوت خطوب ، درس بالنظامية ببغداد والف العدة شرح الإبانة وغيرها ، توفى في حدود سنة خمس وتسعين وأربعمائة ، وأما محمد بن أحمد الشاشي فهو الإمام حافظ المذهب أبو بكر الشاشي مصنف المستظهرى ومؤلف الشافعى شرح الشامل ، صيته الذائع يغنينا عن التبسط في ترجمته وكان معيدا لدرس أبى إسحق الشيرازي ، توفى سنة سبع وخمسمائة عن ثمان وسبعين سنة ودفن في قبر شيخه أبي إسحق . وأما الحسين بن أحمد البغدادي فهو الإمام ، الكبير أبو عبد الله بن البقال الفقيه البارع النظار من أصحاب القاضي أبي الطيب وممن ولى القضاء بحريم دار الخلافة ، توفى سنة سبع وسبعين وأربعمائة عن ست وسبعين سنة . وأما تزيزى بن عبد الملك شيذله فهو الإمام أبو المعالى الجيلى مؤلف البرهان - من أقدم ما ألف
The signatories of this document are the great imams of the Shafi'i school in Baghdad at that time. As for Ibrahim bin Ali al-Firuzabadi, he is the Imam of Imams Abu Ishaq al-Shirazi, author of al-Tanbih, al-Muhadhdhab, al-Nukat, al-Luma', al-Tabsira, al-Mulakhkhas, al-Ma'una, al-Ishara, Tabaqat al-Fuqaha, and other works in fiqh, dialectics, legal disagreement, the two fundamentals, and biographies. The dignity of this Imam in knowledge and piety is unknown only to one whom God does not care for; scholars of all sects have acknowledged his imamate, and his fame suffices for praise. He died in the year 476 AH at the age of 83, and the famous Imam Abu al-Wafa ibn Aqil al-Hanbali performed his washing. As for al-Husayn bin Muhammad al-Tabari, he is the excellent Imam al-Husayn bin Muhammad bin Ali al-Tabari, the grandfather of the Tabaris in the Hijaz, one of the most eminent companions of Imam Abu Ishaq al-Shirazi. Incidents occurred between him and the Hanbalis who affirm letter and sound. He taught at the Nizamiyya in Baghdad and authored al-'Uddah, Sharh al-Ibana, and others. He died around the year 495 AH. As for Muhammad bin Ahmad al-Shashi, he is the Imam, the memorizer of the school, Abu Bakr al-Shashi, author of al-Mustazhiri and al-Shafi'i's Sharh al-Shamil. His widespread fame suffices us from elaborating on his biography. He was a repeater of Abu Ishaq al-Shirazi's lessons. He died in the year 507 AH at the age of 78 and was buried in the grave of his teacher Abu Ishaq. As for al-Husayn bin Ahmad al-Baghdadi, he is the great Imam Abu 'Abdillah ibn al-Baqqal, the excellent jurist and speculative theologian, one of the companions of Qadi Abu al-Tayyib, and among those who served as judge in the Harim Dar al-Khilafa. He died in the year 477 AH at the age of 76. As for 'Azizi bin 'Abd al-Malik Shaydhalla, he is the Imam Abu al-Ma'ali al-Jili, author of al-Burhan—one of the earliest works authored.
Source pages p. 241

Commentary
This passage is a biographical section listing the signatories of the petition. The author identifies them as senior Shafi'i imams in Baghdad. Each biography includes the person's full name, scholarly works, notable positions, and sometimes death dates. Ibrahim al-Firuzabadi is highlighted as Abu Ishaq al-Shirazi, a towering figure. Al-Tabari is noted for conflicts with Hanbalis who affirm letter and sound (i.e., anthropomorphists). Al-Shashi was a revisor of al-Shirazi's work. Al-Baghdadi was a judge. Al-Jili authored al-Burhan. These biographies establish the credibility of the petitioners.

Correction: Ibn Asakir deliberately provides these details to establish the signatories' scholarly authority, thereby strengthening the document's credibility and refuting opponents who might question its provenance.

Biography of Abu Ali al-Asbahani and Closing Remarks
Biographical sketch of Abu Ali al-Asbahani with emphasis on his scholarly authority.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the life and scholarly credentials of Abu Ali al-Asbahani as recorded by Ibn Asakir, and how his biography reinforces the author's argument against anthropomorphism.

Core Idea
Abu Ali al-Asbahani's career exemplifies the fusion of fiqh and kalam in defending tawhid.

Ibn Asakir continues his list of renowned scholars who opposed anthropomorphism by presenting Abu Ali al-Asbahani. This biography details his origins, education under eminent teachers, and his distinguished roles as judge and professor at the Nizamiyya. The passage also highlights his exceptional eloquence and his unmatched sermons on tawhid, further solidifying the author's claim of scholarly consensus.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage and translation
Read through the Arabic text and its literal translation once to get a general sense of the biography.
Pay attention to the flow of information: lineage, education, career, and death.
2
Identify key biographical details
List the key facts: his father's background, his teachers, the positions he held (judge and teacher), and his return to Baghdad.
Notice the author's personal note 'while I was there' which adds authenticity.
3
Examine the description of his qualities
Focus on how Ibn Asakir describes his beauty, eloquence, and theoretical insight. Why would these be mentioned?
These qualities reinforce his authority and reliability as a witness.
4
Understand the significance of his sermons on tawhid
The text says he was peerless in sermons on tawhid (monotheism). Consider why this is important for the author's purpose.
It shows he was a leading defender of correct Islamic doctrine.
5
Reflect on the closing remarks
Note the death date and the mention of Ibn al-Najjar's biography. How does this add credibility?
Citing a well-known historian like Ibn al-Najjar strengthens the historical record.

⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ومنهم شيخنا الإمام أبو على الحسن بن سليمان الأصبهاني رحمه الله كان أبوه أديباً من أهل النهروان يعرف بابن الفتى فسكن أصبهان وكان يؤدب أولاد نظام الملك وولد له الحسن باصبهان فتأدب بأبيه ، وتفقه على الإمام أبي بكر بن محمد بن ثابت الخجندی مدرس مدرسة نظام الملك بأصبهان وعلى غيره وولى قضاء خوزستان ثم ولى تدريس المدرسة النظامية ببغداد إذ كنت بها وكان ممن يملأ العين جمالا والأذن بيانا ويربى على أقرانه فى النظر ، لأنه كان أفصحهم لسانا وخرج عن بغداد ثم عاد إليها وقد شرع في عقد مجالس التذكير وأنشأ الخطب في التوحيد التي هو فيها عديم النظير وظهر له القول التام ولكن لم تمتد له فيه الأيام فورد على بعد عودى من بغداد كتاب الشريف أبى المعمر المبارك ابن أحمد بن عبد العزيز الأنصارى فذكر أنه توفى فى يوم الاثنين الخامس من شوال سنة خمس وعشرين وخمسماية . وبلغنى عن غير أبي المعمر أنه سئل في في علوم القرآن - كان فقيهاً نظارا واعظا حلو الكلام بارعا صنف كتباً كثيرة وجمع لنفسه مشيخة ، قدم بغداد قبل الأربعين وأربعمائة وبها توفى سنة أربع وتسعين وأربعمائة ودفن مقابل تربة الإمام أبي إسحق الشيرازي رحمهم الله تعالى ترجمه ابن النجار في ذيل تاريخ بغداد ترجمة وافية وترجمه المصنف
Among them is our teacher, the Imam Abu 'Ali al-Hasan bin Sulayman al-Asbahani—may God have mercy on him. His father was a literary man from the people of al-Nahrawan, known as Ibn al-Fata, and he settled in Isfahan. He tutored the children of Nizam al-Mulk, and al-Hasan was born to him in Isfahan. He was educated by his father, and studied fiqh under Imam Abu Bakr bin Muhammad bin Thabit al-Khujandi, teacher of Nizam al-Mulk's school in Isfahan, and under others. He served as judge of Khuzestan, then as teacher at the Nizamiyya school in Baghdad while I was there. He was one who filled the eye with beauty and the ear with eloquence, and surpassed his peers in theoretical insight because he was the most eloquent in speech. He left Baghdad, then returned to it and began holding admonition sessions and delivering sermons on tawhid in which he was peerless. He produced a complete discourse, but his days did not extend long. After my return from Baghdad, a letter came from al-Sharif Abu al-Mu'ammar al-Mubarak bin Ahmad bin 'Abd al-'Aziz al-Ansari, mentioning that he died on Monday, the fifth of Shawwal, 525 AH. I was told by other than Abu al-Mu'ammar that he was asked about... in sciences of the Qur'an—he was a jurist, a speculative theologian, a preacher, sweet of speech, excellent. He authored many books and compiled a mashyakha for himself. He came to Baghdad before 440 AH and died there in 494 AH, and was buried opposite the grave of Imam Abu Ishaq al-Shirazi—may God Almighty have mercy on them. Ibn al-Najjar translated him in the supplement to Tarikh Baghdad with a comprehensive biography, and the author also translated him.
Source pages p. 242

Commentary
This passage is a biographical sketch of Abu Ali al-Asbahani, a distinguished Shafi'i scholar. It provides details of his lineage, education, teaching career, and eloquence. Notably, he was a judge and taught at the Nizamiyya. He delivered sermons on tawhid, indicating his role in combating anthropomorphism. The author includes his death date and mentions that Ibn al-Najjar wrote a biography of him. The passage ends with a note that the author (Ibn Asakir) also included a biography. This section serves to further legitimize the petition's signatories.

Biography of Abu Ali al-Hasan ibn Sulayman al-Isbahani
Biography of a Hanafi-Ash'ari scholar with education and death report.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to describe the life, education, and scholarly contributions of Abu Ali al-Isbahani as recorded by Ibn 'Asakir.

Core Idea
A scholar's biography reveals the chain of learning and the legacy of Islamic scholarship.

This passage from Ibn 'Asakir's Tabyin Kidhb al-Muftari presents a biographical sketch of a prominent Hanafi-Ash'ari scholar. It traces his lineage, education, professional appointments, and his eventual return to Baghdad to teach and preach. The passage also records his death date, providing a precise historical marker.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once, then the English translation. Familiarize yourself with the flow of the biography.
Notice the structure: lineage, education, career, character, death.
2
Identify the scholar's lineage and early education
Note that his father was a tutor to the sons of Nizam al-Mulk, and how this influenced his upbringing. He was educated by his father and later studied fiqh under prominent teachers.
The father's role is important for understanding the scholar's social standing.
3
Trace his career progression
Follow his appointments: judge of Khuzestan, then teacher at the Nizamiyya school in Baghdad. Recognize that Ibn 'Asakir was present in Baghdad during his tenure.
The Nizamiyya was a prestigious institution; this appointment indicates his scholarly rank.
4
Reflect on his scholarly contributions
He delivered sermons on tawhid and was known for his eloquence and unmatched works. Consider why his discourse was considered 'complete' and why his days were not prolonged.
He died shortly after beginning his major scholarly output.
5
Note the death report
The exact date (5 Shawwal 525 AH) and the source (a letter from Sharif Abu al-Ma'mar) are given. This anchors the biography in historical time.
Death reports are common in biographical entries to provide closure.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ومنهم شيخنا الإمام أبو على الحسن بن سليمان الأصبهاني رحمه الله كان أبوه أديباً من أهل النهروان يعرف بابن الفتى فسكن أصبهان وكان يؤدب أولاد نظام الملك وولد له الحسن باصبهان فتأدب بأبيه ، وتفقه على الإمام أبي بكر بن محمد بن ثابت الخجندی مدرس مدرسة نظام الملك بأصبهان وعلى غيره وولى قضاء خوزستان ثم ولى تدريس المدرسة النظامية ببغداد إذ كنت بها وكان ممن يملأ العين جمالا والأذن بيانا ويربى على أقرانه فى النظر ، لأنه كان أفصحهم لسانا وخرج عن بغداد ثم عاد إليها وقد شرع في عقد مجالس التذكير وأنشأ الخطب في التوحيد التي هو فيها عديم النظير وظهر له القول التام ولكن لم تمتد له فيه الأيام فورد على بعد عودى من بغداد كتاب الشريف أبى المعمر المبارك ابن أحمد بن عبد العزيز الأنصارى فذكر أنه توفى فى يوم الاثنين الخامس من شوال سنة خمس وعشرين وخمسماية.
Among them is our teacher, the Imam Abu 'Ali al-Hasan ibn Sulayman al-Isbahani, may God have mercy on him. His father was a litterateur from the people of al-Nahrawan, known as Ibn al-Fata, and he settled in Isfahan. He used to tutor the sons of Nizam al-Mulk, and al-Hasan was born to him in Isfahan, and he was educated by his father. He studied fiqh under Imam Abu Bakr ibn Muhammad ibn Thabit al-Khujandi, the teacher of the Nizamiyya school in Isfahan, and under others. He was appointed judge of Khuzestan, then he was appointed to teach at the Nizamiyya school in Baghdad when I was there. He was one who filled the eye with beauty and the ear with eloquence, and he surpassed his peers in theoretical investigation, because he was the most eloquent of them in tongue. He left Baghdad, then returned to it, and he began to hold gatherings of admonition and delivered sermons on tawhid in which he was without peer, and his complete discourse became apparent, but his days were not prolonged in it. Then after my return from Baghdad, the book of al-Sharif Abu al-Ma'mar al-Mubarak ibn Ahmad ibn 'Abd al-'Aziz al-Ansari arrived, mentioning that he died on Monday, the fifth of Shawwal, in the year five hundred and twenty-five (525 AH).
Source pages p. 242

Commentary
This passage is a biographical entry of an Ash'ari scholar, Abu 'Ali al-Isbahani. It begins by stating his lineage: his father was a well-known teacher from al-Nahrawan who tutored the children of the vizier Nizam al-Mulk. Abu 'Ali was born in Isfahan and educated by his father. He studied fiqh under prominent teachers, including Abu Bakr al-Khujandi, and eventually became judge of Khuzestan and later a teacher at the prestigious Nizamiyya school in Baghdad. The author, Ibn 'Asakir, notes that he was present (kuntu biha) when Abu 'Ali was appointed. The scholar is described as exceptionally beautiful, eloquent, and intellectually superior to his peers. He left Baghdad briefly, then returned and began delivering sermons and scholarly discourses on tawhid (divine unity), producing unmatched works. However, his career was cut short. The death date is given as fifth Shawwal 525 AH, reported via Sharif Abu al-Ma'mar. The passage thus provides a standard biographical sketch: lineage, education, positions, character, and death.

Key Terms
الشيخ
الإمام
التفقه
المدرسة النظامية
التوحيد
الوعظ

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some might think Abu 'Ali was a direct student of Nizam al-Mulk or that he studied under him.
Correction: In fact, his father tutored Nizam al-Mulk's sons, and Abu 'Ali studied under other teachers, not Nizam al-Mulk himself.

Checkpoint

D) Supervisor of the mint

Key Takeaway
Abu Ali al-Isbahani was a distinguished Hanafi-Ash'ari scholar, judge, and teacher at the Nizamiyya, known for his eloquence and sermons on tawhid.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Despite his eloquence and unmatched sermons, the scholar's days were not prolonged. What does this remind you about the shortness of life? What is one thing you are procrastinating in your religious learning that you can start today because you may not have tomorrow?
?
This scholar was a product of a chain of teachers: his father, then al-Khujandi, then others. Who is the teacher that has most impacted your Islamic understanding? What are you doing to ensure that the knowledge you receive is passed on to others, just as he passed on his knowledge by teaching?

Biographical Note: A Scholar Buried Near Abu Ishaq al-Shirazi
Brief biography of a jurist and preacher.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the key biographical details of a notable scholar who died in 494 AH and the significance of his burial location.

Core Idea
Burial near a great Imam signals a scholar's own stature.

This short biography, reported from a source other than Abu al-Ma'mar, provides a snapshot of a scholar's career and death. The passage highlights his scholarly attributes, his works, and his burial near the tomb of Imam Abu Ishaq al-Shirazi. It also notes the sources that recorded his life.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage

Look for figh, kalam, preaching, authorship, and compilation of a mashyakha.
3
Note the date and place
Observe his arrival in Baghdad before 440 AH and his death in 494 AH.
4
Understand the significance of burial location
Reflect on why being buried opposite Abu Ishaq al-Shirazi is notable.
Abu Ishaq al-Shirazi was a major Shafi'i scholar.
5

Note that both Ibn al-Najjar and the author (Ibn 'Asakir) wrote biographies of him.

⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وبلغني عن غير أبي المعمر أنه سئل في في علوم القرآن - كان فقيهاً نظارا واعظا حلو الكلام بارعا صنف كتباً كثيرة وجمع لنفسه مشيخة ، قدم بغداد قبل الأربعين وأربعمائة وبها توفى سنة أربع وتسعين وأربعمائة ودفن مقابل تربة الإمام أبي إسحق الشيرازي رحمهم الله تعالى ترجمه ابن النجار في ذيل تاريخ بغداد ترجمة وافية وترجمه المصنف.

He was buried opposite the tomb of Imam Abu Ishaq al-Shirazi, may God have mercy on them. Commentary
This passage is a short biographical notice about an unnamed scholar. It begins with a reported statement that he was asked about Quranic sciences. The scholar is described as a faqih (jurist), nazzar (theological investigator), wa'iz (preacher), sweet of speech, and brilliant. He wrote many books and compiled a list of his teachers (mashyakha). He arrived in Baghdad before 440 AH and died there in 494 AH. He was buried opposite the tomb of Imam Abu Ishaq al-Shirazi. The passage ends by noting that Ibn al-Najjar included a full biography of him in his work Dhayl Tarikh Baghdad, and that the author (Ibn 'Asakir) also wrote a biography. The location of burial and the mention of two biographers indicate the scholar's significance.

A Scholar's Prediction of His Death in Shawwal
Anecdote about a scholar's death sign and burial at Abu Ishaq's tomb.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how this anecdote illustrates the connection between sincere worship, divine acceptance, and a blessed end, as well as the community's veneration of the scholar.

Core Idea
A true sign of accepted worship is a life ended in goodness.

This short but weighty anecdote captures a moment of spiritual insight. A scholar, in one of his gatherings, speaks about the sign of a fast being accepted — and it turns out to be a prophecy of his own death. The story illustrates the connection between sincere worship, divine acceptance, and a blessed end, and it shows the deep affection the people of Baghdad had for him.

Guided Path
1
Read the anecdote
Read the Arabic passage carefully, then its translation. Note that it begins with 'some of his gatherings' — a fragment that places us in a teaching setting.
2
Understand the prediction
Identify what the scholar said about the sign of accepted fasting: 'I will die in Shawwal before being soiled with evil deeds.' Reflect on why dying soon after Ramadan without sin is considered a sign of acceptance.
Shawwal is the month immediately following Ramadan.
3
Observe the fulfillment
The passage confirms that the scholar indeed died in Shawwal after completing the Ramadan fast. This shows the truthfulness of his words and his spiritual state.
4
Reflect on the community's response
Note the unprecedented grief of the people of Baghdad and his burial at the tomb of Shaykh Abu Ishaq. This reflects the high status of the scholar and the impact of his piety.
Consider why such grief might be a sign of the scholar's blessedness.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
بعض مجالسه عن علامة قبول الصوم فقال أن نموت في شوال قبل التلبس بسيء الأعمال فمات في شوال بعد تأدية صوم شهر رمضان وأظهر أهل بغداد عليه من الجزع ما لم يعهد مثله ودفن بتربة الشيخ أبي إسحق.
Some of his gatherings: about the sign of acceptance of fasting, he said, 'I will die in Shawwal before being soiled with evil deeds.' So he died in Shawwal after performing the fast of the month of Ramadan. And the people of Baghdad showed such grief over him as had never been seen, and he was buried in the tomb of Shaykh Abu Ishaq.
Source pages p. 243

Commentary
This passage is a brief anecdote about a scholar (likely the one mentioned in the previous biographical note or a continuation). It begins by noting 'some of his gatherings' (some of his teaching sessions or sermons). In one such gathering, he spoke about the sign that fasting has been accepted (by God). He predicted his own death: 'I will die in Shawwal before being soiled with evil deeds.' That is, he would die immediately after Ramadan without committing sins. The prediction came true: he died in Shawwal after completing the Ramadan fast. The people of Baghdad were grief-stricken to an unprecedented degree, and he was buried in the tomb of Shaykh Abu Ishaq (likely Abu Ishaq al-Shirazi). The anecdote highlights the scholar's piety and the popular affection for him.

قبول الصوم
شوال
تربة
علامة

Key Takeaway
Sincere worship can lead to a blessed end, and the community's grief reflects the scholar's spiritual station.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?
The scholar predicted his death in Shawwal. Do you live each day as if it could be your last? What concrete step will you take today to ensure you do not delay repentance?
?
The people of Baghdad grieved deeply for him. If you died today, would your loved ones see your death as a loss of a righteous person? What one quality should you develop so that your departure leaves a spiritual void?

Biography of Abu Sa'id al-Mihani
Biography of an Ash'ari scholar known for his commentary on khilaf.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the life and scholarly contributions of Abu Sa'id al-Mihani as recorded by Ibn 'Asakir.

Core Idea
Abu Sa'id's commentary on khilaf became the standard reference in the field.

This lesson introduces the biography of Abu Sa'id al-Mihani, an Ash'ari scholar known for his authoritative commentary on legal disagreement (khilaf). His life represents a model of scholarly dedication, from studying in Merv to teaching at the Nizamiyya school in Baghdad. The passage highlights his education, teaching career, and the impact of his work.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scholar
Read the name and epithets. Note his title 'Shaykh Imam' and his fame as author of a commentary on khilaf.
2
Trace his education
Find where he studied fiqh and usul, and under whom. Note the significance of studying usul at an advanced age.
3
Understand his career
See that he served in government, taught at the Nizamiyya multiple times, and influenced many jurists.
4
Assess his legacy
Note his reputation for sound analysis and strong debate, and that his commentary superseded all others.
Ibn 'Asakir personally saw him but did not hear from him.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ومنهم الشيخ الإمام أبو سعيد أسعد بن أبي نصر بن الفضل العمری المیهنی رحمه الله صاحب التعليق المحشو بالتحقيق المبرز في علم الخلاف المشهور في سائر البلدان والاطراف تفقه بمرو على الشيخ الإمام أبي المظفر منصور ابن محمد بن عبد الجبار السمعانى المروزى وقرأ الأصول على كبر السن على شيخنا الإمام أبي عبد الله محمد بن الفضل الفراوى رحمه الله واشتغل بخدمة بعض أسباب السلطان ثم ولى تدريس المدرسة النظامية ببغداد غير مرة وعلق عنه جماعة من الفقهاء . وانتفعوا بطريقته وكان مشهوراً بحسن النظر موصوفاً بقوة الجدل ونسخ بتعليقته سائر التعاليق شاهدته ببغداد ولم أسمع منه شيئا وتوفى بهمذان في سنة سبع وعشرين وخمسماية على ما كتب به أبو المعمر.
Among them is the teacher, the Imam Abu Sa'id As'ad ibn Abi Nasr ibn al-Fadl al-'Umari al-Mihani, may God have mercy on him. He is the author of the commentary filled with verification and preeminent in the science of khilaf (legal disagreement), famous in all countries and regions. He studied fiqh in Merv under the teacher Imam Abu al-Muzaffar Mansur ibn Muhammad ibn 'Abd al-Jabbar al-Sam'ani al-Marwazi, and he read usul (principles of jurisprudence) at an advanced age under our teacher Imam Abu 'Abd Allah Muhammad ibn al-Fadl al-Farawi, may God have mercy on him. He occupied himself in service to some of the sultan's officials, then he was appointed to teach at the Nizamiyya school in Baghdad more than once. A group of jurists made of him/his commentary a source of knowledge; they benefited from his method. He was well-known for sound theoretical analysis, described as strong in debate, and his commentary superseded all other commentaries. I saw him in Baghdad but did not hear anything from him. He died in Hamadan in the year seven and twenty and five hundred (527 AH), according to what Abu al-Ma'mar wrote to me.
Source pages p. 243

Commentary
This passage is a biographical entry for Abu Sa'id al-'Umari al-Mihani, an Ash'ari scholar. It first identifies him by name and notes his famous work: a ta'liq (commentary) on khilaf (legal disagreement), which is filled with verification and is well-known everywhere. His education: he studied fiqh in Merv under Imam Abu al-Muzaffar al-Sam'ani al-Marwazi (a prominent Shafi'i scholar) and later read usul (principles of jurisprudence) under Imam Abu 'Abd Allah al-Farawi at an advanced age. After serving some state officials, he was appointed multiple times to teach at the Nizamiyya school in Baghdad. Many jurists benefited from his method. He was known for good theoretical analysis (nazar) and strong debate skills. His commentary on khilaf became so authoritative that it superseded all other commentaries. The author, Ibn 'Asakir, reports that he saw him in Baghdad but did not hear from him directly. His death date is given as 527 AH, reported by Abu al-Ma'mar. The biography emphasizes his scholarly achievements and teaching positions.

الخلاف
التفقه
الأصول
المدرسة النظامية
حسن النظر
قوة الجدل

B) Imam Abu 'Abd Allah al-Farawi

Biography of Sharif Abu 'Abd Allah al-Maqdisi
Biography of a Maliki/Shafi'i scholar born in Beirut who taught in Baghdad.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the life, education, and scholarly contributions of the noble Imam al-Maqdisi.

Core Idea
A scholar's journey from Beirut to Baghdad, embodying concise, benefit-filled admonition.

This lesson introduces al-Maqdisi, a distinguished scholar who studied in Jerusalem and Mecca and taught in Baghdad. His biography illustrates the traditional path of Islamic learning through personal mentorship and disciplined teaching.

Guided Path
1
Read the biography carefully
Read the Arabic passage and its translation. Notice the key details: his lineage, birth, teachers, and activities.
Pay attention to the description of his admonition sessions.
2
Identify the key events
List the major milestones: birth, meeting teachers, settling in Baghdad, and death.
3
Reflect on the description of his sessions
The passage says his sessions were 'qalilat al-hashw' (little filler) and full of benefits. What does this tell us about his teaching style?
This reflects the method of early scholars.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ومنهم شيخنا الشريف الإمام أبو عبد الله محمد بن أحمد بن یحیی ابن جنى العثمانى الديباجی المقدسی رحمه الله ولد سنة اثنتين وستين وأربعمائة ببيروت من ساحل دمشق ولقى الفقيه أبا الفتح نصر بن إبراهيم المقدسي رحمه الله، ببيت المقدس ، ولزم صاحبه القاضي يحيى بن يحيى المقدسي الذي خلفه في مدرسته بعد خروجه عن بيت المقدس وتفقه أيضاً بالقاضي حسين الطبري نزيل مكة ، وسكن بغداد وكان يفتى بها ويناظر ويذكر ، وكانت مجالس تذكيره قليلة الحشو مشحونة بالفوائد على طريقة تذكير المتقدمين ، وكان كما كتب إليه بعض أهل الفضل متمثلا في حقه بقول بعض الشعراء : مبارك الطلعة ميمونها يصلح للدنيا وللدين كتب إلى الشريف أبو المعمر يذكر أنه مات يوم الأحد السابع عشر من صفر سنة سبع وعشرين وخمسماية.
Among them is our teacher, the noble Imam Abu 'Abd Allah Muhammad ibn Ahmad ibn Yahya ibn Junna al-'Uthmani al-Dibaji al-Maqdisi, may God have mercy on him. He was born in the year four hundred and sixty-two (462 AH) in Beirut, on the coast of Damascus. He met the faqih Abu al-Fath Nasr ibn Ibrahim al-Maqdisi, may God have mercy on him, in Jerusalem, and he kept company with his companion, the judge Yahya ibn Yahya al-Maqdisi, who succeeded him in his school after his departure from Jerusalem. He also studied fiqh under the judge Husayn al-Tabari, a resident of Mecca. He settled in Baghdad, where he gave fatwas, engaged in disputation, and delivered admonitions. His admonition sessions were concise, filled with benefits, following the method of the earlier admonishers. It was as one of the virtuous wrote to him, quoting a poet's words: 'Blessed of countenance, auspicious, fit for this world and for religion.' Al-Sharif Abu al-Ma'mar wrote to me stating that he died on Sunday, the seventeenth of Safar, in the year seven and twenty and five hundred (527 AH).
Source pages p. 243

Commentary
This passage is a biographical entry for the noble scholar al-Maqdisi. It begins with his name, including his title 'al-Sharif' (indicating descent from the Prophet), and his nisbah 'al-Maqdisi' (from Jerusalem). He was born in 462 AH in Beirut. His education: he met the faqih Abu al-Fath al-Maqdisi in Jerusalem and attached himself to his companion, Judge Yahya ibn Yahya al-Maqdisi, who took over the school after Abu al-Fath left Jerusalem. He also studied fiqh under Judge Husayn al-Tabari in Mecca. He then settled in Baghdad, where he issued fatwas, engaged in munazara (theological disputation), and gave tadhkir (admonition). His admonition sessions are described as 'qalilat al-hashw' (little filler), meaning they were to the point and packed with benefits, following the style of the early scholars. A virtuous person wrote to him quoting a poetic verse praising him as blessed and suitable for both worldly and religious affairs. The death date is given as 17 Safar 527 AH, reported by Sharif Abu al-Ma'mar. The biography highlights his role as a teacher and preacher in Baghdad.

الشريف
الفقيه
المناظرة
التذكير
المسائل الفقهية

This passage introduces us to a scholar named Ibn al-Rutbi. Though the biography is cut short, we can see the typical pattern: naming the person, his birthplace, and his teachers. Ibn Asakir uses these details to place the scholar in the chain of knowledge transmission.

The Life and Scholarship of Abu Sa'id As'ad al-Mihani
Ibn Asakir records the biography of As'ad al-Mihani, noting his scholarly achievements and death.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the scholarly profile of Abu Sa'id As'ad al-Mihani, his education, works, teaching career, and his significance in Islamic jurisprudence.

Core Idea
A single commentary that outshone all others: the legacy of As'ad al-Mihani.

This lesson introduces a notable jurist from the 6th Islamic century. Ibn 'Asakir records the biography of As'ad al-Mihani, highlighting his educational background, his famous commentary on legal disagreement, and his teaching appointments at the Nizamiyya school. As you read, notice how the biographer emphasizes both his scholarly achievements and his personal connection.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyse it. Then read the translation. Let the biographer's own rhythm come through before you interpret.
2
Identify key details
Look for al-Mihani's teachers, his famous work, his teaching positions, and the date and place of his death. Note the description of his commentary.
3
Understand the significance of his commentary
The text says his commentary superseded all others. Ask yourself: what does this imply about his scholarly influence and the quality of his work?
4
Reflect on the chain of transmission
Notice the teachers and students mentioned. This shows the scholarly network of the time and how knowledge was passed on.
Ibn 'Asakir himself saw al-Mihani but did not hear from him directly.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ومنهم الشيخ الإمام أبو سعيد أسعد بن أبي نصر بن الفضل العمری المیهني رحمه الله صاحب التعليق المحشو بالتحقيق المبرز في علم الخلاف المشهور في سائر البلدان والاطراف تفقه بمرو على الشيخ الإمام أبي المظفر منصور ابن محمد بن عبد الجبار السمعانى المروزى وقرأ الأصول على كبر السن على شيخنا الإمام أبي عبد الله محمد بن الفضل الفراوى رحمه الله واشتغل بخدمة بعض أسباب السلطان ثم ولى تدريس المدرسة النظامية ببغداد غير مرة وعلق عنه جماعة من الفقهاء . وانتفعوا بطريقته وكان مشهوراً بحسن النظر موصوفاً بقوة الجدل ونسخ بتعليقته سائر التعاليق شاهدته ببغداد ولم أسمع منه شيئا وتوفى بهمذان في سنة سبع وعشرين وخمسماية على ما كتب به إلى أبو المعمر
And among them is the teacher, the Imam, Abu Sa'id As'ad ibn Abi Nasr ibn al-Fadl al-`Umari al-Mihani, may Allah have mercy on him, the author of the commentary filled with verification prominent in the science of legal disagreement, well-known in all cities and regions. He studied fiqh in Marw under the teacher, the Imam, Abu al-Muzaffar Mansur ibn Muhammad ibn `Abd al-Jabbar al-Sam`ani al-Marwazi, and he read the principles (usul) at an advanced age under our teacher, the Imam, Abu `Abd Allah Muhammad ibn al-Fadl al-Farawi, may Allah have mercy on him. He occupied himself with serving some of the sultan's officials, then he was appointed to teach at the Nizamiyya school in Baghdad more than once. A group of jurists took (wrote down) from his commentary and benefited from his method. He was well-known for good insight and described as having strong argumentation. His commentary superseded all other commentaries. I saw him in Baghdad but did not hear anything from him. He died in Hamadan in the year 527 AH, according to what Abu al-Mu`ammar wrote to me.
Source pages p. 243

Commentary
This passage is a biographical entry for the scholar Abu Sa'id As'ad al-Mihani. It begins by identifying him as the author of a famous commentary (ta`liq) on legal disagreement (khalaf), a work distinguished by its verification. It then details his education: he studied fiqh under al-Sam`ani in Marw and later studied usul (principles of jurisprudence) under al-Farawi at an advanced age. The entry notes his service to state officials and his multiple appointments as teacher at the prestigious Nizamiyya school in Baghdad. Many jurists wrote down his commentary and adopted his method. He was renowned for his analytical skill and strength in debate, and his commentary surpassed others. The author, Ibn `Asakir, mentions seeing him in Baghdad but not hearing from him. The biography concludes with his death date, 527 AH, in Hamadan, as reported by Abu al-Mu`ammar.

Key Takeaway

?
The source says his commentary superseded all others because of its verification (tahqiq). In what area of your life are you settling for superficial understanding instead of the kind of verification that leaves a lasting impact? What would it take for you to become the kind of person whose work stands out?
?
He served some officials and then taught at the Nizamiyya. Are you using your position, however small, to serve the deen? Or are you waiting for a perfect opportunity? What is one way you can serve the spread of knowledge today, even if it seems insignificant?

Biography of Sharif Abu 'Abd Allah al-Maqdisi
Ibn Asakir records the biography of al-Sharif Abu 'Abd Allah al-Maqdisi, noting his teachers and scholarly gatherings.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the life and scholarly profile of al-Sharif Abu 'Abd Allah al-Maqdisi as recorded by Ibn Asakir.

Core Idea
A blessed scholar who combined fiqh, fatwa, and concise spiritual reminders.

Ibn Asakir includes the biography of al-Sharif Abu 'Abd Allah al-Maqdisi among his teachers. This passage highlights his birth, his teachers, his scholarly activities in Baghdad, and the distinctive style of his reminder gatherings. The entry also includes a poetic tribute and his death date.

Guided Path
1
Read the biography passage
Read the Arabic passage and its translation to get an overview of al-Maqdisi's life events and scholarly profile.
Notice the structure: birth, teachers, activities, death.
2
Identify his teachers and locations
List the teachers mentioned and the cities where he studied and taught: Beirut, Jerusalem, Baghdad, Mecca.
He studied under Abu al-Fath al-Maqdisi, Yahya al-Maqdisi, and Husayn al-Tabari.
3
Analyze the description of his gatherings
The passage says his gatherings were 'qalilat al-hashw mashhunat bi al-fawa'id' (concise, filled with benefits). Reflect on what this implies about his teaching style.
This follows the method of early scholars (tadhkir al-mutaqaddimin).
4
Reflect on the poetic praise
The verse praises him as blessed and good for both this world and religion. Consider how this summarizes his legacy.
The praise is from some virtuous people, showing his high regard.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ومنهم شيخنا الشريف الإمام أبو عبد الله محمد بن أحمد بن یحیی بن جنى العثمانى الديباجی المقدسی رحمه الله ولد سنة اثنتين وستين وأربعمائة ببيروت من ساحل دمشق ولقى الفقيه أبا الفتح نصر بن إبراهيم المقدسي رحمه الله، ببيت المقدس ، ولزم صاحبه القاضي يحيى بن يحيى المقدسي الذي خلفه في مدرسته بعد خروجه عن بيت المقدس وتفقه أيضاً بالقاضي حسين الطبري نزيل مكة ، وسكن بغداد وكان يفتى بها ويناظر ويذكر ، وكانت مجالس تذكيره قليلة الحشو مشحونة بالفوائد على طريقة تذكير المتقدمين ، وكان كما كتب إليه بعض أهل الفضل متمثلا في حقه بقول بعض الشعراء : مبارك الطلعة ميمونها يصلح للدنيا وللدين كتب إلى الشريف أبو المعمر يذكر أنه مات يوم الأحد السابع عشر من صفر سنة سبع وعشرين وخمسماية
And among them is our teacher, the noble Imam Abu `Abd Allah Muhammad ibn Ahmad ibn Yahya ibn Jani al-`Uthmani al-Dibaji al-Maqdisi, may Allah have mercy on him. He was born in the year 462 AH in Beirut on the coast of Damascus. He met the jurist Abu al-Fath Nasr ibn Ibrahim al-Maqdisi, may Allah have mercy on him, in Jerusalem and accompanied his companion, the judge Yahya ibn Yahya al-Maqdisi, who succeeded him in his school after his departure from Jerusalem. He also studied fiqh under the judge Husayn al-Tabari, a resident of Mecca. He settled in Baghdad and used to issue fatwas, debate, and give reminders. His reminder gatherings were concise, filled with benefits, following the method of the early remindeers. As some virtuous people wrote to him, applying to him the words of a poet: 'Blessed in countenance, auspicious; he is good for this world and religion.' Al-Sharif Abu al-Mu`ammar wrote to me that he died on Sunday, the seventeenth of Safar, in the year 527 AH.
Source pages p. 243

Commentary
This passage is a biographical entry for al-Sharif Abu `Abd Allah al-Maqdisi. It begins with his birth in 462 AH in Beirut. It then lists his teachers: he met the jurist Abu al-Fath al-Maqdisi in Jerusalem, accompanied the judge Yahya ibn Yahya al-Maqdisi, and also studied under judge Husayn al-Tabari. He settled in Baghdad and became a scholar who issued fatwas, engaged in debates, and gave spiritual reminders. His gatherings are described as concise and beneficial, following the style of early scholars. The entry quotes a poetic praise written to him, commending his blessed presence and his suitability for both worldly and religious affairs. It concludes with his death date, 17 Safar 527 AH, reported by Abu al-Mu`ammar.

Biography of Qadi Abu al-'Abbas Ibn al-Rutbi
Ibn Asakir records the biography of Qadi Abu al-'Abbas Ibn al-Rutbi, noting his judgeships and teaching.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the life and scholarly career of Qadi Abu al-'Abbas Ibn al-Rutbi as recorded by Ibn Asakir, including his teachers, judicial roles, and scholarly reputation.

Core Idea
A scholar's journey from asceticism to judgeship exemplifies pious service.

Ibn Asakir continues his biographical dictionary with the entry of Qadi Abu al-'Abbas Ibn al-Rutbi, a Shafi'i jurist who rose from humble beginnings to become a judge and tutor to caliphs. This passage illustrates the path of a scholar who combined deep learning with public service, earning praise for his eloquence and mastery of legal debate.

Guided Path
1
Read the biography
Read the Arabic passage once without analysis, then read the translation. Let the narrative flow before interpreting details.
Pay attention to the sequence of events and the list of positions.
2
Identify key stages
Note his teachers (Abu Ishaq al-Shirazi, Abu Bakr al-Shashi, al-Khujandi), travels, the shift from asceticism to public service, and his offices.
The positions are explicitly enumerated: judge, hisba, endowments, tombs, leading prayer, tutoring.
3
Examine the anecdote
Read the remark by al-Maqdisi and the jurists about his discourse triumphing over As'ad's. Consider what this tells us about his scholarly status.
This shows he was highly regarded for his debating skill.
4
Reflect on the biography's theme
Ask yourself: What does this biography teach about the ideal scholar? How does Ibn al-Rutbi's life balance asceticism and worldly engagement?
The biography portrays a scholar who remains effective and esteemed despite holding power.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ومنهم شيخنا القاضى الإمام أبو العباس أحمد بن سلامة بن عبيد الله بن مخلد المعروف بابن الرطبي رحمه الله من أهل كرخ بعقوبا تفقه بالشيخ أبي إسحق إبراهيم بن عنى الشيرازى بشيراز ثم لزم الشيخ الإمام أبا بكر الشاشي بعد وفاة الشيخ أبي إسحق ، ورحل إلى ن وتفقه بالإمام أبي بكر محمد الحسين الخجندى مدرس النظامية بأصبهان ، وسمع بها شيئاً من الحديث ورجع إلى العراق وكان يتزهد فى ابتداء أمره ثم تقدم عند الخلفاء وولى قضاء نهر معلا ببغداد والحسبة والنظر فى الوقوف وفي أمر ترب الخلفاء والصلاة بأمير المؤمنين المسترشد بالله رحمه الله وتأديب ولده أبي جعفر المنصور الراشد بالله وكان مقدماً فى المعرفة بالمذهب والخلاف ، حسن المناظرة حلو العبارة . سمعت الشيخ أبا عبد الله المقدسى وقال له بعض الفقهاء لقد ظهر اليوم كلام القاضى أبى العباس على كلام الشيخ الإمام أسعد ومتى لم يظهر . كلام القاضي على كلامه ، مات ليلة الاثنين مستهل رجب سنة وعشرين وخمساية ودفن في تربة الشيخ أبي إسحق الشيرازي كتب إلى بذلك أبو المعمر
And among them is our teacher, the judge, the Imam Abu al-`Abbas Ahmad ibn Salama ibn `Ubayd Allah ibn Makhlad known as Ibn al-Rutbi, may Allah have mercy on him, from the people of Karkh Ya`quba. He studied fiqh under Shaykh Abu Ishaq Ibrahim ibn `Ani al-Shirazi in Shiraz. Then he accompanied the teacher, the Imam, Abu Bakr al-Shashi after the death of Shaykh Abu Ishaq. He traveled to [Nishapur?] and studied fiqh under the Imam Abu Bakr Muhammad al-Husayn al-Khujandi, teacher at the Nizamiyya in Isfahan. He heard some hadith there and returned to Iraq. He adopted asceticism at the beginning of his career, then he gained favor with the caliphs and was appointed judge of Nahr Ma`la in Baghdad, and also held the office of hisba (market inspector), supervisor of endowments, and in charge of the tombs of the caliphs, as well as leading the prayer for the Commander of the Faithful al-Mustarshid bi-Allah, may Allah have mercy on him, and teaching his son Abu Ja`far al-Mansur al-Rashid bi-Allah. He was advanced in knowledge of both the school (madhhab) and legal disagreement (khilaf), excellent in debating, and sweet in expression. I heard Shaykh Abu `Abd Allah al-Maqdisi say—and some jurists said to him: 'Today the speech of Qadi Abu al-`Abbas has triumphed over the speech of Shaykh Imam As'ad; whenever does the Qadi's speech not triumph over his?' He died on the night of Monday at the beginning of Rajab in the year 520 AH and was buried in the tomb of Shaykh Abu Ishaq al-Shirazi. Abu al-Mu`ammar wrote to me with that.
Source pages p. 244

Commentary
This passage is a biographical entry for Qadi Abu al-`Abbas Ibn al-Rutbi. It begins with his origin from Karkh Ya`quba. It details his study of fiqh under Abu Ishaq al-Shirazi in Shiraz, and then his accompanying Abu Bakr al-Shashi after al-Shirazi's death. He also traveled to study under al-Khujandi in Isfahan and heard hadith there. He returned to Iraq and initially practiced asceticism, but later rose in status with the caliphs and held multiple important positions: judge of Nahr Ma`la, market inspector, supervisor of endowments and caliphal tombs, and leading the prayer for Caliph al-Mustarshid, as well as tutoring his son. He was well-versed in the Shafi'i school and legal controversy, skilled in debate, and eloquent. The entry includes a saying from al-Maqdisi and other jurists praising his dominance in debate over As'ad al-Mihani. It concludes with his death on the 1st of Rajab 520 AH and his burial in the tomb of Abu Ishaq al-Shirazi, as reported by Abu al-Mu`ammar.

Key Takeaway

?
This scholar was praised for his 'sweet expression' and excellence in debate. When you speak about your faith, do you strive to be clear, kind, and compelling? Or do you often remain silent out of laziness or fear? This week, seek one opportunity to articulate a truth of Islam to someone in need of guidance, and prepare for it by reviewing the lesson's source text as a model.
?
Ibn al-Rutbi taught the caliph's son and led the prayer for the ruler. Are you using your knowledge to influence those in authority around you—your employer, your community leaders, your parents? Or do you shy away from that responsibility? Write down the name of one person in a position of authority whom you can advise or support with Islamic principles before this month ends.

Life of Imam Ibn Asakir
